Jiading 104

Conference on Relief in War Zones. The Jiading Branch of the War Zone Relief Committee held its 15th meeting on the 26th. Vice Chairman Pan Zhixing presided over the meeting. He reported that disaster victims repeatedly came to the meeting in groups to petition, waiting anxiously for funds, but the provincial allocation of funds totaled only 30,000 yuan. The Shanghai Fellow Association sent 15,000 yuan of surplus relief funds, the County Party Department allocated 400 yuan of national salvation funds, and more than 3,000 yuan of flood relief righteous funds will also be allocated to the meeting soon. It was decided at the meeting that the Shanghai War Zone Post-Disaster Committee will establish a temporary epidemic hospital in Jiading, and the administrative expenses will be borne by the county. The committee will subsidize 300 yuan. The remaining 15,000 yuan of relief funds from the Shanghai Fellow Association will be entrusted to the committee for donation and loan separately. 3,000 yuan will be used to comfort the bereaved families of the deceased, 4,500 yuan will be allocated to the Food Management Committee, and the price per stone will be reduced by four corners. The remaining funds will be allocated by the committee to supplement the insufficient funds for various loans.

Rickshaw pullers strike. There were originally more than 280 rickshaws in the city, but more than 240 were lost in the war. The Di, Ji, and Ren companies, considering the heavy losses, jointly increased the rent. The original price was 52 cents per rickshaw per month, but it was increased to 20 cents per rickshaw per day. The rickshaw pullers asked for a reduction to no avail, so they went on strike unanimously on the morning of the 26th. The County Chamber of Commerce mediated and convened both parties in the afternoon to persuade them to make concessions, but there was no result.

Suzhou 105

Execution of Lake Bandit Who Robbed a Steamer. The lake bandit Hu Bolin, from Songjiang, 21 years old, colluded with a large gang of bandits on May 2nd of this year to rob the Shenhu Banzhou small steamer and shot and killed one male and one female passenger. Subsequently, detectives from the First Water Police District arrested the bandit at the Yunzhou Hotel in the French Concession of Shanghai, interrogated him and confirmed the facts, and transferred him to the Suzhou-Songjiang Water Bandit Suppression Headquarters. After a clear retrial, he was sentenced to death and taken to the Wangshudun execution ground on the 25th for execution by shooting.

Wuxi 106

A Young Woman Commits Suicide in a Wuxi Hotel. A female guest from Shanghai arrived at the Wuxi Hotel on Gongyun Bridge at more than two o'clock on the night of the 23rd. She was dressed exquisitely and signed herself as Ms. Zou, 23 years old, from the Sichuan academic community. On the 25th, she said that she would go to Nanjing, and bought letter paper and envelopes, closed the door to write a letter. After about four hours, she did not come out. The waiter heard intermittent moans from the room, and peeped through the crack, only to see Zou Yurong looking miserable. He rushed into the room to check and saw an empty bottle of Nalian sleeping pills under the bed, knowing that she was poisoned. He rushed her to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, but they said that she was deeply poisoned and it would be difficult to save her. The lady could speak various dialects such as Sichuan, Shanghai, and Guangdong, and her clothes were all silk. It seemed that she had received higher education. However, there was a note on each of her left and right wrists, which read, "Bad luck, better to die." The handwriting was delicate, so the reason for her suicide could not be known.

Wuxi Chamber of Commerce Opposes Special Business Tax. More than 80 industries in Wuxi, including oil, beans, cotton yarn, cloth, paper, tea, and north-south goods, believe that the special business tax in the guise of likin in Jiangsu Province has been set to be implemented and levied on July 1st. At this time of financial recovery and economic depression, not only are merchants unable to cope, but it also violates central laws and regulations. They held an emergency temporary meeting in the Chamber of Commerce the day before yesterday and decided to organize a tax law research committee and send telegrams to home and abroad requesting public judgment. The telegram reads as follows: "The loss from abolishing likin and increasing taxes has already been compensated. The nature of both business and consumption taxes is already supplementary, and according to the original likin abolition plan of 1928, the Ministry of Finance, based on the resolutions of the National Financial Conference and the likin abolition telegram, abolished all domestic likin and various transit taxes similar to likin nationwide, and at the same time established special consumption taxes (that is, the unified tax currently administered by the central government) and business taxes administered by the provinces to compensate. Now Jiangsu Province is implementing a special business tax in the guise of likin, which has fundamentally overturned the original likin abolition plan of 1928. After likin abolition, the customs duties added by the central government, the unified taxes administered domestically, and the business taxes administered by the provinces are all without foundation. At this time, the war in Shanghai has just stopped, and the market has plummeted. Merchants are struggling in pain, and considering the government's difficulties, they dare not rush to ask for relief. How can they bear more burdens? Therefore, an emergency temporary meeting of various industries was held on the 24th, and it was decided that if the special business tax in Jiangsu Province is implemented and levied, in order to maintain the central government's original likin abolition plan and to express its determination, it will have to suspend all unified and business taxes first, and send telegrams to home and abroad requesting public judgment. We hereby telegraphically state first, and respectfully request your public judgment. Wuxi County Chamber of Commerce kowtows." It is also heard that the Department of Finance, in view of the enthusiastic opposition of merchants in various places, has room for maneuver and no longer insists on implementing and levying on July 1st. However, the provincial treasury is in dire straits, and if no other means of compensation are devised, it will be difficult to maintain. Yesterday, it specially invited Yu Xiaochuan, Qian Sunqing, Wang Jingting and others, standing members of the Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, to negotiate in the province today (27th) for a thorough discussion on the two sample measures contributed by the Chamber of Commerce Federation, such as rectifying two months of rent throughout the province, and levying business license tax and pre-paying a quarter of taxes.

Establishment of the Famine Relief Committee. After the lean years in this county, it also encountered the war in Shanghai. The social economy collapsed, and the trend of robbing rice in the villages occurred from time to time. The County Chamber of Commerce and the County Party Department, in view of this, specially invited more than 60 leaders from all walks of life to a meeting in the County Chamber of Commerce at 3 pm yesterday, and publicly elected Qian Sunqing as chairman to discuss the establishment of the Famine Relief Committee. The main points are as follows: (1) Named Wuxi Temporary Famine Relief Committee, (2) All directors of more than 120 people, 27 people were proposed from the directors to form an executive board, (3) Li Tiping, Chen Chuande, Qian Sunqing and other nine people were elected as directors of the general affairs section, Li Tiping and Qian Sunqing were the directors, Chen Zhanru, Cai Jian, Yang Hanxi, Gui W臣 and other nine people were elected as directors of the fundraising section, Chen Zhanru and Cai Jian were the directors, Gu Shuzhi, Hua Yinchun, Hua Jianji, Xu Yongyi and other nine people were elected as directors of the investigation section, Gu Shuzhi and Hua Yinchun were the directors, and Li Tiping and Qian Sunqing were elected as the directors of the executive board, (4) Allocated 20,000 yuan for the accumulated grain and 10,000 yuan for the embankment repair, and the rest was to strive for 2.5 cents of construction per mu donation from the provincial government to stay in Xiji relief, (5) The meeting place was set up in the County Chamber of Commerce, and the board of directors met every Tuesday at 2 pm. All the suffering of each was reported in detail to the meeting by the directors to coordinate relief measures. The meeting ended near 6 pm.

Roving Bandits Rob a Fast Boat. The Qingyang Kaicheng fast boat, yesterday (25th) at about 5 pm, was sailing from the city to Qing. Maintaining the Resumption of Jimei. Since the Jimei pawnshop stopped operating, the party and government agencies, in order to maintain the economy of the common people, organized the board of directors and requested the Industrial Department of the County Government to add 100,000 yuan of capital within three months, together with the 200,000 yuan of capital, to officially resume the operation of the pawnshop. Before the capital was fully raised, the pawnshop was ordered to maintain the pawn redemption, and the department approved it. If the pawnshop collected the redemption money and挪用it for other purposes, the county was allowed to send personnel to stop it. After receiving the order, the agencies decided that before the capital was fully raised, the money released by the pawnshop would be used as capital, and the pawnshop would resume operation yesterday (25th), with a limit of two yuan per ticket. At about 9 am, the pawnshop was extremely crowded. The agencies also sent personnel to supervise, but the Sheng pawnshop owner denied the resumption of operation and insisted on closing down. However, the agencies decided that it was based on the order of the Industrial Department and would take effective measures to allow the long-term resumption of operation.

Change of Director of the Construction Bureau. Wei Yuanzhong, Director of the Danyang Construction Bureau, has been in office for nearly four years. He has now been transferred to Nantong by order of the Department. The vacancy has been filled by Dong's appointment of Zhang Youbin, a technical officer.

Representatives Go to the Province to Request Instructions on Donations. The Nantong County Defense Team needs 240,000 yuan for annual expenses. Jiangsu Province's New Prison Plan. The Ministry of Justice has concrete plans for improving old prisons and establishing new prisons, which will be implemented first in Jiangsu Province. The Jiangsu Higher Court has ordered all district prisons to comply. The new prison plan is to set up a new prison in each district. All county prisons in the district will be reformed and become branches of the new prison. All prisoners with sentences of more than three years must be sent to the new prison for execution. County prison guards will be renamed branch prison chiefs and concurrently serve as detention center directors. The improvement design will be handled by the current prison directors. The new prison planning is as follows: (1) Each prison is located in Jiangning, with a capacity of 1,500 people. The subordinate branches are Jiangpu, Jurong, Lishui, Gaochun, and Liuhe. (2) One juvenile prison will be set up in Jiangning and Tongshan respectively. The Jiangning prison will accommodate first-time offenders under the age of 25 from various counties in Jiangnan, with a capacity of 1,000 people. The Tongshan prison will accommodate first-time offenders under the age of 25 from various counties in Jiangbei, with a capacity of 500 people. (3) The second prison is located in Shanghai, with a capacity of 2,000 people. The subordinate branches are Qingpu, Chongming, Jiading, Baoshan, Chuansha, and Nanhui. (4) The third prison is located in Wuxian, with a capacity of 1,000 people. The subordinate branches are Wujiang, Kunshan, Taicang, and Changshu. (5) The fourth prison is located in Nantong, with a capacity of 700 people. The subordinate branches are Qidong, Haimen, and Rugao. (6) The fifth prison is located in Zhenjiang, with a capacity of 1,000 people. The subordinate branches are Yangzhou, Danyang, Liyang, and Jintan.

Jiashan 110

A Yellow-Surnamed Son Was Kidnapped and Escaped Home. The son of the Yellow Yuansheng deli shop in western Jiashan County, aged only 28, is now studying at the county's junior high school outside the East Gate, leaving early and returning late. The day before yesterday, the student did not return until dark. His family sent people to search everywhere, but there was no trace. Unexpectedly, the student suddenly returned yesterday afternoon. When his family asked him what happened, the student said that after school that day, he was watching soccer at the public sports field. Two bandits dragged him to the side of a boat parked next to the sports field, forced him to get on the boat, covered his eyes, and stuffed his throat. The boat sailed away quickly. On the boat, one bandit asked who he was. He told the truth. The bandit said that he had made a mistake and wanted to kidnap the son of a Gu in the city. Because of this, they were not very guarded against him, so he was able to escape.

Jiaxing 111

The Plague Intensifies. Cholera has been discovered inside and outside Jiaxing City for the past ten days. Patients vomit and have diarrhea, and then their muscles cramp. Many die before they can be treated. In recent days, due to the irregular weather, the plague has intensified. In the past two days, the survey of residents in the city and suburbs who died of the plague has shown that there are dozens of people dying every day, mostly middle-aged people. Now, Chinese medicine has researched a first-aid method for the treatment of those who are newly infected. The hospital has purchased preventive drugs through the Health Association and entrusted them to doctors for free injection. Local people have also organized a plague prevention and rescue team to provide rescue.

Guarding Police Lost Their Guns. Jiaxing Vagrant Training Institute has one resident patrol captain and eight police officers to guard it. Unexpectedly, the police guard room of the institute lost a Russian-style gun the day before yesterday. The County Public Security Bureau sent police to search the institute, but they found nothing. Jin Sheng, a worker at the civilian training institute next door, was suspected of having a grudge against the patrol captain Zhang Guanghao. Zhang reported to Director Xu, who detained Jin Sheng in the Public Security Bureau for questioning. He also sent police to search the civilian training institute, but nothing was found. After questioning by the County Bureau, Jin Sheng knew that he had been falsely accused due to a grudge, so he was released. Director Xu has now detained and investigated the patrol captain Zhang Guangjing.

[Education News Highlights]

Ministry of Education Orders Short-Term Literacy Education 113

The Ministry of Education's order to all provinces and cities to implement literacy education and the first phase of compulsory education implementation measures was reported in yesterday's newspaper. Herewith, we publish the "Outline of Short-Term Compulsory Education Implementation Measures" and the full text of the Ministry's order separately as follows. It is said that the said order was drafted by five key members of the Ministry of Education and repeatedly revised before it was approved and issued. This shows the Ministry's emphasis on literacy education. The order states that since the late Qing Dynasty, enlightened people in our country have been aware of the necessity of popularizing education, and have spared no effort to advocate for compulsory education. The party platform also has a provision for "vigorously promoting the popularization of education," and the Provisional Constitution of the Tutelage Period even has a special article stating that "children who have reached school age should all receive compulsory education." The reason is that our country's national level is still immature. Whether we want to catch up with countries with higher national levels in terms of foreign affairs, or implement the minimum level of local autonomy in terms of domestic affairs, we must vigorously implement compulsory education and strive to popularize education.

However, for more than twenty years, advocacy and promotion have not been lacking in effort, and the duration of four years of primary school is not considered difficult to implement. However, judging from the facts, the national primary education statistics for the 18th year of the Republic show that only 17% of school-age children are enrolled. The goal of popularizing education seems far away. The reason why it has taken so long and required so much effort with so little effect is that the funding required for four years of compulsory education is in the tens of millions, and the number of teachers needed is in the millions, which is still a far cry from the actual state of the country's financial resources and existing teaching staff.

The Ministry is ordered by the Party and the country to urgently implement compulsory education. In order to adapt to the environment and facilitate promotion, it has specially formulated two types of implementation measures: the "Short-Term Compulsory Education Implementation Measures" and the "Outline of the First Phase of Compulsory Education Implementation Measures." The former is only for one year and is used to educate older, out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen. Therefore, it is called short-term compulsory education. The latter is still for four years, which is no different from what has been advocated and promoted in the past. The two measures are issued at the same time so that all provinces, counties, cities, and special districts directly under the Executive Yuan can implement them simultaneously, or give priority to short-term compulsory education, according to the amount of their funding and teachers, in order to achieve rapid results.

In terms of funding, a teacher in short-term compulsory education teaches three classes of older, out-of-school children in the morning, afternoon, and evening, giving each class two hours of education. With 40 students per class, 120 children can graduate in one year. Compared with three teachers giving full-day education to two classes of primary school children, also with 40 students per class, 80 children can graduate in four years. The difference in the amount of funding required is no less than a ratio of 1 to 18. In terms of teachers, the curriculum for short-term compulsory education is only literacy and simple arithmetic, which is easy to teach, and those who know a little reading and arithmetic can do it well. Compared with the complex curriculum of primary school, which is difficult to teach, and which cannot be handled without professional teacher training, the difficulty of finding teachers is also different. Since funding is saved and teachers are easier to find, it is not difficult to achieve universalization even if the level is shallow.

In areas where financial resources are limited to short-term compulsory education, school-age children under the age of ten cannot increase their enrollment opportunities. However, given the current weakness of the national economy, only one or two out of ten families can afford to send their children to receive four years of compulsory education. Even if primary schools are everywhere, they are all unable to enroll. Moreover, older children have a richer learning ability, and the effect of one year may sometimes be no different from that of a six-year-old who receives four years of education. If short-term compulsory education can be implemented so that all out-of-school children over the age of ten in the country can receive one year of education, the increase in national standards and efficiency will be self-evident. In all countries of the world, the duration of compulsory education is gradually being extended, while our country is turning from four years to one year. On the surface, it seems to be different from others, not advancing but retreating. However, in reality, given the lack of funding and teachers in our country, there is no way to promote the popularization of education. It is like the poor without a foothold seeing the vast mansions of others, and being endlessly envious. However, rather than hoping for a one-in-a-million chance and delaying action, it is better to build a thatched hut that can shelter from the wind and rain. In the future, as the national level gradually increases and the social economy rises with it, when funding and teachers can be solved, not only can four years of compulsory education be expected to be popularized, but it can also be extended to six, eight, or even more than ten years, surpassing all countries in the world. This is not impossible.

Since the measures have just been finalized, I am deeply afraid that the matter is unique and that people in the country will not understand the meaning, or even doubt the righteousness, or even fail to implement them effectively and delay the grand plan. Therefore, the intention of short-term compulsory education is repeatedly explained, hoping for common understanding.

The two measures are hereby sent with the order. The said department is requested to refer to the local situation and earnestly comply with the implementation from the 21st year of the Republic. Those who cannot implement the first phase of compulsory education at the same time should give priority to implementing the short-term compulsory education measures and submit a concrete plan within one month of receiving the document to report for the record and implement it on schedule without delay. This is of utmost importance. This order distributes two copies each of the Short-Term Compulsory Education Implementation Measures and the Outline of the First Phase of Compulsory Education Implementation Measures (the first phase of compulsory education measures were reported in yesterday's newspaper).

Outline of Short-Term Compulsory Education Implementation Measures 114

Article 1: During the period when funding is difficult and primary schools are not easy to popularize, in order to help older out-of-school children, short-term compulsory education implementation measures are specially formulated to facilitate promotion.

Article 2: The implementation of short-term compulsory education is based on townships, towns, and public offices. Provinces, cities, administrative regions, special districts, and counties should designate appropriate locations as short-term compulsory education experimental zones for testing and demonstration, and give priority to short-term compulsory education.

Article 3: Short-term compulsory education is implemented in specially established short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes added to primary schools and improved private schools. All agencies, groups, and individuals have the obligation to promote or establish short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes.

Article 4: In the short-term compulsory education experimental zone, all older out-of-school children aged ten to sixteen should enter short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes to receive short-term compulsory education.

Article 5: The plans for implementing short-term compulsory education in each county and city shall be approved by the competent education administrative agency, reported to the education department for review, and forwarded to the Ministry of Education for record. In the special administrative districts directly under the Executive Yuan, they shall be reported directly to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 6: The funds required for the implementation of short-term compulsory education shall be raised locally in principle. If local funds are difficult, a request may be submitted to the superior agency for subsidies, but it shall not exceed one-half. The funds required for those established by various levels of agencies such as provinces, cities, districts, and counties shall be included in the education budget by the respective levels of agencies.

Article 7: Short-term primary schools and short-term primary school classes shall be exempt from tuition fees. All books and school supplies shall also be provided by the school in principle.

Article 8: The school buildings of short-term primary schools shall make full use of public places such as temples, charity halls, public offices, ancestral halls, and various agencies, or borrow surplus houses from factories, shops, and private residences.

Article 9: Short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes adopt a class-sharing teaching system (morning, afternoon, evening), with two hours of instruction per day (each hour is calculated as sixty minutes), a study period of one year, and at least 270 days of class per year (540 hours).

Article 10: Short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes aim at literacy. The curriculum includes one subject: the national language, and focuses on phonetic symbols. The content includes common sense courses such as history, geography, civics, arithmetic, and nature. The curriculum standards are set separately. Those who are not familiar with phonetic symbols may be temporarily exempted from teaching phonetic symbols.

Article 11: The principals of short-term primary schools shall be hired by the competent education administrative agency or the establisher and reported to the superior education administrative agency for record.

Article 12: In addition to hiring qualified personnel to serve as faculty and staff in short-term primary schools, the following personnel should be fully utilized: (1) student teachers from local normal schools or rural normal schools who have reached the internship stage; (2) private school teachers who have received considerable training and can serve as substitute teachers; (3) local civil servants; (4) local personnel with considerable education; (5) volunteers who serve as teachers and fulfill their obligations.

Article 13: Short-term primary school classes attached to primary schools or private schools should make full use of the original primary school and private school teachers.

Article 14: Private groups or individuals who establish short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes, and volunteers who serve as teachers in short-term primary schools, should be specially rewarded by the local education administrative agency. The reward measures shall be separately determined by the local competent education administrative agency. Article 15: In principle, each teacher in a short-term primary school or short-term primary school class shall be responsible for three classes. If the teacher in a short-term primary school class is concurrently served by a primary school teacher or a private school teacher, each person shall be responsible for one or two classes.

Article 16: A short-term primary school with three classes shall have one principal who also serves as a teacher. A school with four to six classes shall have one principal who also serves as a teacher, one teacher or concurrent teacher, or one assistant teacher, and so on by analogy.

Article 17: The number of students in each class in a short-term primary school or short-term primary school class shall be no more than 40.

Article 18: Older out-of-school children should be forced to enter short-term primary schools or short-term primary school classes. Those who are not physically healthy may postpone or be exempted from schooling. The measures for compulsory or deferred or exempted schooling shall be separately stipulated by the competent education administrative agency according to local conditions, and shall be reported to the superior education administrative agency for record.

Article 19: The local autonomous organs shall, in conjunction with the personnel of the Public Security Bureau, complete the investigation of older out-of-school children two months before the start of each semester and report to the provincial and municipal education administrative agencies for verification.

Article 20: The local autonomous organs, the personnel of the Public Security Bureau, and the local gentry and elders shall be responsible for supervising and ordering older out-of-school children to enroll in school.

Article 21: The county mayor and the director of the Public Security Bureau shall have the responsibility to assist in the implementation of short-term compulsory education. Those who fail to assist or obstruct it shall be punished according to the seriousness of the circumstances. The measures shall be stipulated by the Provincial Department of Education, submitted to the Provincial Government for decision, and consulted with the Ministry of Education and the Ministry of Interior for record and implementation.

Article 22: The measures for evaluating the performance of short-term compulsory education shall be stipulated by the education administrative agencies of provinces, cities, and districts, and submitted to the Ministry of Education for record and implementation.

Article 23: Those who have special circumstances and cannot implement short-term compulsory education at one time may submit a request to the superior agency for approval to postpone it and forward it to the Ministry of Education for record.

Article 24: These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Ministry of Education and shall be repealed when primary school education is popularized throughout the country.

(2) A Glimpse of the Olympic Village 121

Architectural Excellence Unsurpassed. The Olympic Village, which brings together athletes from 51 countries, has now been completed. This truly international village has a total of 550 beautiful and exquisite small houses, which are no less than an exhibition of model cities. The roofs are painted blue, and the walls are white and pink. Each house has two rooms, and each room can accommodate two people. The room is equipped with two spring beds and a washstand, all of which are from famous American factories. The preparatory committee has separately stipulated the positions of the athletes of various countries. The largest of the cafeterias is the American group, which can accommodate 21 people. All the tables and chairs are rattan furniture for summer use. The meals for each athlete are selected according to the preferences of each country. The Japanese group is about half a mile from the front, east of Turkey, Yugoslavia, Hungary, west of Belgium, and behind France, Germany, Switzerland, the Netherlands, Sweden, Lithuania, and Finland. The village divides its area by language. For example, the United Kingdom, the United States, Canada, and Australia, etc., use English as a group, which is in the northeast corner of the village. The committee members of various countries stay in the general affairs building at the main entrance. At the entrance, there are residences for athletes from Mexico, Spain, Cuba, etc. The village is equipped with a fire brigade, which patrols day and night. The telephone bureau uses switchboard operators from various countries, and there is also a hospital. In the middle of the village, there is an amusement park and an open-air theater. In front of the main entrance, 55 national flags of participating countries are clustered. Among them, the most famous French and Spanish cuisines in the world have hired famous chefs to come to the meeting to cook. The athletes who have arrived are all drinking and eating wildly, and those who are on the way and have not arrived are also salivating at the news.

(4) India Hopes to Win Field Hockey Championship 123

Football will disappear in India. The Indian field hockey team attending the World Games this time has a total of 17 players, along with the team leader, Mr. and Mrs. Lin Bai, and the swimmer Malik, a total of 20 people. The team stayed in Japan for ten days and set off from Yokohama on the Ryudamaru on the 24th. The team performed their magical skills in Japan, defeating the Japanese team by 22 to 0. The mystery of their technology was praised by everyone. According to the team leader, Lin Bai, the strength of the country's field hockey is as follows: The Indian field hockey team's attendance at the World Games began at the 8th Paris Games in 1924. Now, a comprehensive conference is held every two years in the country, and it is particularly enthusiastic about local teams. Records are updated one after another and have long exceeded world standards. The Far East Conference has persuaded the country to join, but due to limited funds, it has not been able to send more players. This team is the holder of the previous World Championship. Among the players selected this time, there are only four old players. Indian football, which was most popular on the 21st, is now almost extinct. Most people have abandoned it and practiced field hockey. The reason why Indian field hockey is so strong is that Indians do not have the habit of smoking or drinking, so their eyesight is particularly sharp, and they are particularly effective in handling white balls. They have reached the upper level in terms of hitting stick skills and defensive work. Although there are strong German enemies at this conference, they are confident that they can definitely keep the championship.

In addition, some Indian track and field and swimming athletes have already arrived in the United States. The schedule of the field hockey team was slightly delayed. It was originally scheduled to stay in Japan for a week, but it has been delayed for ten days.

Records of Knocking the Bell in the Ancient Temple (36) 126

— Bu Chu Ting Cao Zhaifu

Thirty-nine, it's really funny to think about it carefully. It's the same Analects. The way I used to read it made me feel that there was nothing wrong with the Sage's book. Now, if I read it in a different way, I feel that every sentence needs to be re-evaluated. I am extremely remorseful. Why didn't I doubt the things that should have been doubted at all? However, fortunately, I have now received Mr. Zhu's guidance. From now on, I will not easily let go of even a single sentence in the books of the ancients. I remember someone said: "Learning is about knowing how to doubt: Great doubt leads to great progress: Small doubt leads to small progress: No doubt leads to no progress." I should reuse and use this word "doubt" heavily.

This time, when I read the Analects, I couldn't help but laugh when I read the passage about Gongshan Furao rebelling in Fei. When Confucius wanted to collude with the rebels, Zilu was unhappy. Confucius said, "Am I not a gourd? How can I hang here without eating?" Since you know you need to eat, why do you say, "A gentleman seeks the Way, not food"?

Forty. A-Yang ran to the door and gently told me: "They say that Mr. Song, whom you invited, is not capable and that he copied answers in the city." I asked him where he heard it from. He said that Wang Er's sister-in-law heard it from someone. I went to ask Wang Er's sister-in-law. She said that the tailor's clerk, Lao Qian, said it. So I went to ask Lao Qian. Lao Qian said that the carpenter, Wu, passed it on. By the time I tracked it down to the carpenter, Wu, and inquired in detail, I realized that the rumor was created by the bricklayer, Lao Xu. He's still making trouble here!

I traced the source of the rumor and returned to the temple to tell Mr. Zhu. But how could I be presumptuous? I thought about it and didn't know how to speak. Suddenly, the little brother ran over and said to Mr. Zhu without hiding anything, "Brother! People in the village say that you copied answers in the city and that you were last." The innocent and lively little brother, how could he speak so carelessly? Why don't I have his frankness and courage? He says everything that should be said.

"This rumor was created by the bricklayer, Lao Xu. I have already found out the truth." As soon as the little brother finished speaking, I explained the origin of the rumor in order to let Mr. Zhu know that Lao Xu deliberately spread the rumor so that he could feel more comforted in his heart.

Mr. Zhu said, "Lao Xu is not spreading rumors. It is true that I copied answers in the city and was last. He probably investigated it on the spot."

Miscellaneous Skills

Enlightenment 127

Whether it's science, philosophy, or literature, all require effort on the word "enlightenment." What is called enlightenment? It is to derive a new path from the most ordinary materials.

Seeing fruit falling, understanding gravity; seeing a kettle boiling, understanding the steam engine; such earth-shattering divine enlightenment is worth commemorating forever!

"Constantly calling out to Xiaoyu, why? Only so that Tanlang recognizes the voice." These are fragrant and seductive verses; however, a certain virtuous elder broke through Zen secrets from these two lines.

"How can one bear that glance of her autumn eyes as she departs?" This is a lyric from the *Romance of the Western Chamber*; however, it is recorded in the sayings of National Master Hongjue, who also broke through Zen secrets from this line.

Therefore, when Lady Gongsun danced with swords, good calligraphers understood the method of using the brush; when Chef Ding dissected oxen for twelve years without dulling the blade, those who cultivate life understood the secret to preventing illness; as long as one is good at enlightenment, one can derive a new life from anything.

There are two exquisite lines in the *Selections of Refined Literature*: "Stone embraces jade, and the mountain shines. River contains pearls, and the water charms." Some people have gained insight into the principles of nourishing life from these two lines. Why do we often see young people with flesh not covering bones and blood not moisturizing skin? It is because the stone does not embrace jade, the river does not contain pearls; naturally, the mountain loses its brilliance, and the river loses its charm.

Duke Wenrui of Tongcheng, Zhang, heard Xunzhai say, roughly: In the stems of orchids and peonies, there must be a drop of dew; if this dewdrop is eaten by insects, the flower will wither. In the early morning, when carefully observing the newly emerged bamboo shoots, there must be several dewdrops at their ends; when the sun rises, the dew will gather and return to the roots, and reappear in the evening. People's primordial energy is also like dewdrops, and so on.

Young men and women! In this tide of flesh, you must have your own conviction, protect your dewdrops, and not let them be eaten by insects; this is the principle. Whenever your hearts are uncertain, please recite repeatedly: "Stone embraces jade, and the mountain shines. River contains pearls, and the water charms"; only stop reciting when your heart has conviction.

"Card Game" Under the Guidance of the Japanese Army Ministry 128

— With Heart

Readers, upon seeing the three words "card game," may immediately think of gambling cards in the countryside, or imported playing cards, but the Japanese card game is not that thing.

Japan originally had two kinds of card games. One is called "Hanafuda," about the same size as poker cards, with words and flowers written on them, mostly playthings for girls. The other is the cards sold by candy sellers on the streets and alleys to trick children. These cards have pictures of people fighting or animals, etc. The seller shakes a bell, gathers many children, and they all look at the pictures and listen to the stories in the pictures. He tells one story and changes the card. At that point, he takes out candy and sells it to the children, who listen to him while holding candy in their mouths. He also earns money.

This kind of card game under the guidance of the Japanese Army Ministry is similar to the second type, but the nature is different. These cards depict soldiers who died in battle in the three northeastern provinces or Shanghai, along with the ferocious and ugly appearances of "Chinese people." The stories told are about the bravery of a certain sergeant in killing the enemy and his honorable death in battle, and how the "Chinese people" are ferocious, unreasonable, and deserving of death! Japanese people must love their country and prepare for war, and so on. The Japanese military strictly guides and controls those engaged in this business. Currently, there are 2,000 people doing this business in Tokyo alone, and more than 20,000 throughout the country. The ambition of the Japanese nation and the intentions of the Japanese military (the representative body of the warlords) can be imagined. (But rewarded)

The Story of Tobacco 129

— Wang Yi Wu

Tobacco has now spread throughout the world, and many people smoke it. However, its history is not very long. Like opium, it was first discovered in the Ming Dynasty, and it was also not a domestic product. It was initially brought into China from Luzon, and later China began to cultivate it. Gradually, it spread throughout the provinces. It is also known as "Danbagu" or "tobacco grass," about three feet tall, with blue-green flowers in the shape of a funnel. The leaves are used to make tobacco, so it is commonly called tobacco grass, which can be made into various types of tobacco. The most popular cigarettes now are one of these types. The other day, I happened to be talking to a friend, Mr. So-and-so, when I heard a story saying that tobacco did indeed only exist in the Ming Dynasty. But it was not introduced from a foreign country. At that time, there was a man named Shi who was betrothed to a woman named Ma. Before the wedding ceremony could take place, Ma suddenly died. Shi was very grieved and vowed never to marry for the rest of his life, crying at Ma's tomb morning and evening, regardless of wind, frost, rain, or snow, without interruption. A kind of grass grew on the tomb, just like planted tobacco. At that time, Shi naturally did not know it was tobacco, but he felt a strange fragrance. One day, because he was so grief-stricken, he suddenly felt dizzy and had a stomachache, and fell to the ground in front of the tomb, unable to get up. He casually picked a leaf and put it in his nostril. Before long, he was no longer dizzy or in pain, but instead felt refreshed. When others found out, they all said that it was a transformation of his blood and tears. Whenever anyone had a disease, they would pick a leaf and eat it as medicine, and it would always cure them immediately. Thus, the story spread, and everyone regarded it as an immortal herb. They planted it, and gradually the planting became widespread, and it became tobacco. In the beginning, opium was also very precious. Siam had used it as tribute, and only the emperor could enjoy it. Emperor Shenzong of the Ming Dynasty loved it the most and became addicted to it. But when China began to cultivate it itself, it became extremely democratized and turned into a raging flood. Tobacco has narcotic properties and can relieve fatigue, so people smoke it even more widely and quickly. In fact, it is also a poison, containing nicotine, which is very harmful to health. Except for China, which absolutely does not prohibit it, other countries have bans on it for minors.

Preparations for the Chinese Art Exhibition in Berlin (Part 2) 130

— Baishi

In the spring of the twentieth year [of the Republic], the Chinese painter Liu Haisu was invited by the Chinese Academy of the city of Frankfurt, Germany, to lecture on Chinese painting. He also held a Chinese modern painting exhibition at the Frankfurt Art Museum, which was moved to Heidelberg in June. The impact at that time was greater than expected. This was because in the early spring of that year, the Japanese had held a large-scale exhibition in Berlin, so Europeans felt that Oriental art was merely imitating Western art superficially and had not shown its unique characteristics. But when they saw the Chinese modern painting exhibition, they were surprised and praised it endlessly. This was because its simplicity and naturalness, devoid of artificiality, was different from the Japanese works that were labored and fraudulent. The embassy saw that German newspapers were also carrying articles about the need to hold a Chinese modern painting exhibition in Berlin, so they telegraphed to urge Liu to go to Berlin. They formally negotiated with the Prussian Academy of Arts and the Oriental Art Society, and had detailed discussions with oriental scholars, professors at the University of Berlin such as Komeru and Hewrey, the vice president of the Academy of Arts Professor Armer Adolf, and the professor of the Polytechnic University, Barschimen. Finally, the embassy formally agreed with the German side to hold the exhibition in February 1934, using the Prussian Academy of Arts as the exhibition site, and recommended ten German committee members: one representative from the German Foreign Ministry, the chairman of the German Oriental Art Association and former German ambassador to Japan, Dr. Scharvu, the vice chairman of the German Oriental Art Association, Dr. Klenprei, the secretary general of the German Oriental Art Association, the curator of the Oriental Museum and professor at the University of Berlin, Dr. Komeru, the deputy secretary general of the German Oriental Art Association and the director of the National Museum, Kong William, the professor of the Berlin University of Technology and government architectural consultant, Bai Shumen, the curator of the National Art Library and professor at the University of Berlin, Dr. Krachou, the chief accountant of the German Oriental Art Association, Dr. Silverberg, the deputy chief accountant of the German Oriental Art Association, Count Heitou, and the secretary general of the Prussian Academy of Arts and professor at the University of Berlin, Dr. Armer Adolf.

These negotiations took several twists and turns. Once the outline was in place, Liu began to vigorously advocate for artists in the country to work together to achieve success, so as not to let the Japanese usurp the position of master of the Orient.

Respect for Virtue and Age of Elder Sanyuan 131

— Zhenwu

Elder Sanyuan, Mr. Chen Boyan, is peerless in his morality and writing in the current era. Old literati in the country regard him as a great master within the nation. In recent years, he has secluded himself in Mount Lu, where his cultivation is deep. He is already eighty years old. I heard that his solitary birthday celebration is approaching. Famous scholars and worthies intend to celebrate the elder's birthday and are competing to compose poems and articles. Soon, those dazzling compositions will glorify the Southeast region, making it a grand event in the Chinese literary world. Yesterday, I saw a congratulatory couplet handwritten by Mr. Li Liejun, expressing the utmost respect for the virtuous and venerable. The couplet reads:

A long life is naturally an auspicious omen among men.

Great virtue is worthy of being a teacher to the world.

Seeking Kissing Talent 132

— Ying Dai

According to news from New York, a sound expert named Mr. Ray Kelley is seeking a young couple who are good at kissing. Seeking talent is not unusual in itself, but seeking kissing talent is something we have never heard of. He is seeking this kind of talent to produce a sound film scene. His standard for selection is that the couple can only have their lips touching when they kiss, and the sound of the lips touching is recorded by radio. From an artistic point of view, Mr. Kelley's purpose is to study the sound of kissing. When he was studying it, he used an oak stopper to rub on a piece of glass coated with rosin, wanting to use it to replace the sound of kissing, but the sound produced was completely different from kissing, so he had to seek a young couple who were good at kissing.

Impressions of Qingdao (Middle) 133

— He Gongchao

A Shandong man in his fifties stood at the iron gate of the underground chamber, soliciting people to take a tour. I spent three "Mao tickets" to hire him as a guide. Stepping down the stone steps into the underground chamber, I felt a chill on my body, as if entering late autumn. In a narrow, long tunnel made of cement, it was so dark that you couldn't see your fingers, and the ground was wet. If it weren't for a lantern and a small wind lamp to illuminate the way, we really couldn't have moved an inch. As he walked, he pointed out this room and that room, explaining this and that to us. On the left wall of the wounded soldiers' room, there were many bloody handprints. These were left by German wounded soldiers when the Japanese army attacked this fort. I wonder if these wounded soldiers eventually died in this gloomy and desolate basement, or were able to safely withdraw and return to their homeland to live a peaceful life again. These things can no longer be asked, and I'm afraid even the "guide" wouldn't know. Further on, there was a room that he said was used by German expatriate women and children to take refuge during the war, because at that time, bullets were raining down around the fort, and it was extremely dangerous to live outside. Immediately, a scene of mothers and children embracing each other in fear and trembling appeared in my mind. Having experienced the disaster of the Zhabei battle, like a startled bird, I involuntarily trembled again here!

Japanese Bathhouses. Qingdao's bathhouses all have women's bathhouses attached, and all the facilities are the same as those for men. This has given Chinese women, who have never paid much attention to cleanliness, more opportunities to bathe, which is commendable. But Japanese bathhouses have another advantage: that is, the price is particularly cheap, allowing everyone to develop the habit of frequent bathing.

Walking into a Japanese bathhouse, men and women part ways and enter through separate doors. You have to bring your own towel and soap. First, pay the bill (only six cents per person), and then go to bathe. Inside, there is a pool. First, use a basin to scoop water and wipe your whole body clean, then soak in the pool to remove all the dirt, and you're done.

A Record of Life in the Military (93) 134

— Seeking Happiness Studio Owner

Episode Eleven: Peeking at the Official Banners in a Remote County, Scolding the Mean Currents of the Crowd

Although Fourth Master Wu was busy with this big affair, he took advantage of being associated with these two noble guests to return to his hometown and feel very proud. He intended to show off his talent and boast of his glory, and would never shirk the slightest bit of laziness, nor feel the slightest bit of fatigue. At this time, his energy became stronger with use, and he even put in extra effort to inspect each room again to see if all the arrangements were complete. After looking, he admired his own orderliness and felt even more pleased. He became even less inclined to sleep and strolled outside. He saw Qin the accountant in the accounting room, accompanying several bailiffs from the county government, talking and chatting. He guessed that they must have come to inquire about the news, so he approached to exaggerate a little more for the public to know. He puffed out his big belly, entered the room, pretended to be tipsy, and laughed loudly, saying, "Oh, Accountant Qin, what are you talking about with these gentlemen? Could it be that you are talking about me behind my back?" Qin the accountant and the others hurriedly stood up, smiled apologetically, and offered him a seat, saying, "Fourth Master, you went to the provincial capital and came back with these two important figures. We heard that there is even a big commander among them. His official position must be very high. We thought, now that Fourth Master has met benefactors, he will surely be promoted." Fourth Master sat down proudly and chuckled, saying, "I knew you would say that I was doing a good job. To be honest, my trip to the provincial capital was a lucky opportunity. I got to know this amazing Commander An. His title has the characters 'jade' above and 'field' below. When we started talking about family matters, I found out that he was from Anjia Village, the most famous village in our neighboring county. I even have some distant relatives from his side. This gentleman graduated from Peking University and is accomplished in both literary and military affairs. I also heard that he is related to Grand Marshal Ye by marriage, so Grand Marshal Ye sent him to our county to handle the pacification work and establish an army. When he has recruited enough people, he will return to the province and have a good chance of becoming a military governor. I met this gentleman by chance, and he thought highly of me and insisted on having me help him. He promised me the position of chief of staff, entrusting me with all matters, big and small. He truly listens to everything I say and follows every plan I make. I don't know why we get along so well."

Gold Standard Continues to Decline 135

With a fluctuation of ten taels. Yesterday, the gold standard continued to weaken, with violent waves and panic among traders, making it difficult to predict. There were ten taels of fluctuation throughout the day, later falling about three taels. It was initially stable, and the silver market did not move. Afterward, the price rose by six or seven taels. At noon, there was a sudden drop, because a major player dumped long positions, and Hengxing also seemed to have sold, causing a weakening. The price plummeted by eight or nine taels in an instant, finally breaking the 750 tael mark. As for foreign exchange, it was still peaceful, with the market fluctuating around 50 taels. In short, people were confused and uncertain, and finally settled within 50 taels. The details of the market situation are recorded below:

Weakness Before Noon Closes: Opening at 751 taels and three mace in the early morning, slightly up by two cash. However, the public telegram for silver prices remained the same, while the private telegram rose by one-eighth. When it fell back to 49 taels, it was bought by Hengyu, Yuanmao, Yongtongchang, and others to cover positions, and the price rose by four taels to 53 taels. However, HSBC released October U.S. dollars at 30.0625 yuan, and Hengchang, Yongshunli, and others sold, causing a decline of two taels. At 9:15, it was 51 taels. Then, the bank absorbed September British gold at 93.75, and Mitsui absorbed October U.S. dollars from 30 yuan to 29.9375 yuan. As more buyers entered the market, Yuankang, Xianghengchang, Yonglai bought in, reaching 55 taels at 9:30. British and American banks did not change their rates, remaining at 4.5 taels. In a moment, it rose by more than two taels, because Zhifeng, Yongfutai, Hengyuan, Dayong, Yuanmao, Yongyuanheng, Yuantai, and others showed strong buying interest, mainly because more U.S. dollars were settled. The July rate was only 29.5 yuan, September 8.125, and Mitsui absorbed August 6.25 and October 8.75, reaching 56 taels and eight mace at 9:50. Later, Qianchang, Hongli, Dadecheng, Hengchangyong, Bingxing, and others sold, causing a drop of four taels. At 10:20, it was 52.5 taels. Afterward, it rose sharply, as Daxing, Yongfuyu, Hongkang, Yonghongxing, Hongli, Xiexing, Yongtongchang, Shunli, Wanxing, Yuanmaoyuyu, and others competed to buy in succession, causing the market price to rise frequently by more than four taels. From 10:30 to 11:30, there was a fluctuation of more than one tael, until 11:45, when it reached 57 taels and one mace. In an instant, a sudden storm appeared, because Yifeng, Yonghengyu, and others representing Yufengyong, old longs exited the market. Hengxing, Bingxing, Yongfeng, Dadecheng, Hongli, Tongchun, Tongtaichang, and others followed suit, and the exchange rate was flat. In just over ten minutes, it plummeted by nine taels, with only one tael of consolidation in an instant, until 11:56-57, finally reaching 48 taels. At this time, Daxing, Yonghengxing, and Bingxing bought in, jumping up by three taels in one minute to 51 taels, but the closing price was calculated at 49 taels, and the selling pressure did not cease. Ordinary retail investors hurriedly closed out their positions, causing it to drop to 46-47 taels. Fuxingyong and others dragged it in, raising it again by two or three taels to 49 taels and some cash.

Resulting in a Drop of 2 Taels and 8 Mace: The aftermarket opened at 48.5 taels. Yuanxingyong, Tongtaichang, and others bought in, reaching 49 taels and eight mace. Zhifengyong, Fuyu Shunli, and others sold again, causing a decline of more than two taels, reaching 47 taels. At 2:20, the buying side seemed diligent, and Citibank cabled in U.S. dollar prices for July and August, calculated at 75. Maijiali also absorbed July at 6.875. Guangbang Yifeng, Yuanmaoyong, Zhifengyong, Yuankangxiang, and others bought in, presenting a good situation, breaking through 50 taels. At 2:45, it was 51 taels and seven mace. Afterward, Hengxing Yifeng Yonglai exited, Huabi released September U.S. dollars at 8.75, and HSBC released October British gold at 1.7875, reaching 48 taels and one mace at 3:00. Hongli Yifeng bought in, pulling up two or three taels, and it was 50 taels and nine cash. Suddenly, it went down again, because Hengyu, Fuyu, Fuxingyong, Hengchangyong, Dadecheng, and others sold a lot, as the U.S. dollar seemed to loosen, with October settling at 30 yuan. At 3:30, it fell to 47 taels for the second time. In an instant, Bingxing and others dragged it in, and at 4:00, it was 49 taels and six mace. HSBC absorbed July U.S. dollars at 29.75 yuan. Afterward, Fuyu Qianchangxiang and general retail customers hurriedly spat it out, and the price fell by another tael. At 4:20, it was 48 taels. By the time the market closed at 4:30, it was 48 taels and three mace, continuing to fall by 2 taels and 8 mace compared to last Saturday. After the closing, it was done again at around 49 taels. Goods were traded at a premium of seven cash. According to the daily maximum of 57 taels and one mace and the minimum of 47 taels, there was a difference of 10 taels and one cash. Counting the difference, it was plus nine taels and seven and a half cash.

Quotation Suppressed by 72-73 Taels: The quoted price was still 820 taels, because the U.S. dollar did not change, and the premium was 64-65 taels, then 71-72 taels. In the afternoon, it was 71 taels to 70 taels, then the premium was 73 taels, then 68-69 taels. In the end, it was 72 taels, three taels more than last weekend. The Guangdong gang sold more than 1,000 contracts and bought 600 contracts. The total number of contracts traded by each firm by the end of last weekend was approximately 19,000, slightly fewer than the previous one by about 1,000, it is said.

Due to the securities settlement for this month approaching, it was anticipated that a large amount of cash would be released. However, as the demand was not robust, speculators with unique ideas engaged in short selling, exploiting people's psychology. This led to an unprecedented low of nine-tenths of a cent the day before yesterday. By yesterday morning, the situation reversed, and the market gradually improved. As a result, there was a slight increase of half a cent between the two markets. The interbank lending rate gradually rose slightly and was very tight, indicating a potential rise in credit.

Slight Increase in Interbank Lending Rates: The morning interbank lending rate for "foreign exchange" was 6.9025 cents, and the afternoon rate was 6.90375 cents. Yesterday, it rose another cent, totaling 1.3 cents. The morning and afternoon rates were the same, with no changes. Yarn and Cotton Market Trend: Rise Followed by Decline 140

The cotton yarn market experienced an initial rise followed by a decline, with a relatively calm trend. This contrasts with the instability of the previous day. The reason is that the trend is such that when prices rise, new short sellers increase, and no single entity can sustain the price. However, most people in Shanghai believe that the bottom has been reached and are keen to buy, providing strong upward momentum. Overall, the domestic economy is depleted, rural areas are declining, and people's livelihoods are suffering, leading to a significant reduction in cotton yarn consumption. In addition, Japanese merchants are competing to sell at particularly low prices, making it even more difficult for Chinese yarn. However, a major player has recently switched from short to long positions, temporarily restraining the market. The afternoon market suddenly weakened.

After the Exchange Session, the Market Weakened: At the opening of the Exchange session, American cotton was flat, and the situation in Guangdong waters was tense. Each month fell by six or seven qian in the first two or three rounds. Due to the firmness of the cotton market, it rose again by six, seven, or eight qian. As a result, each month rose by three to six qian. In the afternoon, news spread that manufacturers were hedging, causing the market to decline round by round, with each month falling by one, two, or four qian. The total trading volume for the day was 31,100 bales. It was found that Gengfeng sold 2,650 bales, Taichang 950 bales, Yida 800 bales, Dachang 700 bales, Yukang 1,100 bales, and Mingde 1,500 bales. Changfeng bought 1,800 bales, Rongxing 800 bales, and Xincheng 850 bales. The closing prices are listed below:

Cotton Merchants Tend to Take Long Positions 141

The cotton market trend is relatively stable, and most people tend to take long positions, buying and holding. This is because the torrential rise in the Yangtze River's water level is a cause for concern, and there is talk that the deal for the US cotton to be sold on credit to our country may not go through. As a result, the situation in the market is becoming tighter, but actual business remains sluggish. Factories have no demand. As for the matter of buying US cotton on credit, all the contracts and procedures are quite troublesome and cannot be resolved in a moment. However, it is not a problem for the market. It was found that from last year to April of this year, imports of foreign cotton have already reached 1.2 million bales. Whether or not this 600,000 bale deal is successful does not have a special relationship in fact. The afternoon market showed slight signs of weakness, probably due to the easing of gold prices.

Flour Mills Incessantly Issuing 145

Yesterday's flour market, after the morning opening, saw market conditions for each month generally stable. Foreign wheat prices were good, up to 0.14 yuan, and the weather was cold, keeping people calm. Prices were up about 0.01 yuan compared to the previous weekend. However, small and medium-sized factories and Fuxin mills continuously issued offers, totaling about 70,000 to 80,000 bags. By the afternoon opening, prices were initially stable, but the attitude of major factories had changed, and they continuously issued offers for both near and distant periods, causing the market to decline sharply. Observing the subsequent steps, it is feared that it will be difficult to be optimistic, as current sales have not been strong and factories are competing to issue endlessly. As a result, July fell by a small amount of 0.025 yuan compared to the previous weekend, August fell by 0.075 yuan, September fell by 0.01 yuan, October fell by 0.0125 yuan, and November fell by 0.075 yuan.

Sharp Decline in Wheat Futures Market 146

Yesterday's wheat futures market saw prices remain stable, with foreign wheat quotes rising by about 0.24 yuan, keeping outside investors quite stable. However, Datong and Xinfeng and other firms took advantage of this good opportunity to gradually issue offers on all their long positions, causing market conditions to be stable but stagnant. By the afternoon opening, the market plunged again, with Dingtai mills gradually issuing their long positions. In addition, the weather had turned clear, making investors more apprehensive. July fell sharply step by step, while August also fell. The decline in distant periods was smaller. As a result, July fell by 0.09 yuan compared to the previous weekend, August fell by 0.07 yuan, September fell by 0.05 yuan, October fell by 0.03 yuan, and the rest were not opened. The spot wheat market remained stable, as Fuxin Huafeng and other mills still had demand, stabilizing sentiment. Lai wheat opened at 2.94 taels, Anding wheat at 2.90 taels, Hengjing wheat at 2.95 taels, Shuangfeng wheat at 2.96 taels, and Huojiaqiao wheat at 2.80 taels, Baihegang wheat at 2.90 taels, totaling more than 1,400 bags.

French Firms Stockpiling Silk and Tea on the Cheap for Long-Term Gains 149

Prices Will Fall to 90 Taels

Recently, Japanese silk waste (i.e., silk scraps) has been relentlessly sold cheaply in European and American markets, regardless of cost, selling as soon as a price is offered. This has caused our country's silk waste sales to be almost completely taken over, and the market has plummeted, with no one inquiring. European firms are taking advantage of this to stockpile cheaply. Yesterday, firms such as Xinfu continued to buy 20 dan of Wuxi silk factory silk waste at a price that is about to fall to 90 taels, a decline of 50-60 taels compared to last year.
