Local News

City Chamber of Commerce Cables Foreign Envoys to Negotiate on Northeast Tariffs 154

Requests Recognition of Japanese as Principal Party

Due to the Japanese seizing our Northeast tariffs by using a puppet state, the City Chamber of Commerce has cabled the British, American, French, and Italian envoys in Beijing, requesting serious negotiations. The cable reads: "The seizure of customs duties from the three northeastern provinces and the Dalian Customs, located in the Japanese leased territory, by the Manchurian puppet state created by the Japanese, has caused serious concern among creditors, both Chinese and foreign. The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs claims that this is a matter for the Manchurian government, but publicly expresses sympathy for this action. The Dalian Customs Commissioner, Mr. Fukumoto, openly admits that his actions were prompted by warnings from responsible Japanese authorities, further proving that this was directed by the Japanese. As the three northeastern provinces are purely under Japanese military occupation, the so-called important officials of the Manchurian state are concurrently serving as personnel of the Kwantung Army and consuls, and have become integrated with Japan. This action is merely intended to pressure China and its allies with financial disputes by negotiating with the so-called Manchurian state, thereby achieving de facto recognition and undermining the purpose of the Nine-Power Treaty. We respectfully request that all allies recognize that the Japanese are the principal party in this matter, conduct serious negotiations, maintain the unified customs system, and prevent its destruction. As Japan is the creator of the Manchurian state and a creditor with customs guarantees, it cannot be allowed to evade or deny responsibility." Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce.

Yangtze River Flooding Causes Disaster 155

Ganzhou and Hunan Areas Already Submerged

Flood Relief Committee Discusses Measures Yesterday

This spring, the Yangtze River has experienced continuous rain, causing the river to rise significantly. Last month, the river rose to 32.5 feet in Hankou, causing widespread panic. The tragic scene of last year's submersion is being repeated this year. The engineering department of the Flood Relief Committee has allocated 660,000 yuan for disaster relief to build long embankments to prevent flooding. However, due to continuous torrential rains, the Yangtze River has risen several more feet, and Ganzhou and Hunan areas have already been submerged. The following is a report based on what our reporters have learned:

Central Hunan Submerged: Yesterday, our local office received a telegram from Hunan, stating that on the 26th, Changsha experienced continuous heavy rain and the river rose sharply, exceeding 35 feet. The river in Changsha has submerged the shore, and the Nissin Company branch has moved to Xiangtan. Warehouses in lower areas have already been flooded. In the Shashi area, the river level was even with the riverbank on the 26th. If it rises further, the riverbank will also be submerged. Currently, various shipping companies and warehouses are moving goods to higher ground. Yiyang and Changde were also submerged in floodwaters on the 26th.

Ganzhou and Xunzhou Roads Blocked: On the 26th, the water level in Jiujiang was 37 feet, almost level with the riverbank. Due to continuous heavy rain and rising water, the dikes along the Shuanglin, Changhu, Guangfu, Anle, and Shangfu rivers in Ganzhou and Fu County have been breached in several places by floodwaters. Countless homes and fields have been submerged. The Nanzun road has been completely blocked by floodwaters and is impassable.

Recent Conditions in Anhui and Hubei: The water level in Anqing in northern Anhui reached 33 feet 5 inches yesterday, while the water level in Wuhu in southern Anhui reached 33 feet 6 inches. The engineering department is accelerating the construction of flood prevention embankments and increasing the number of inspectors to prevent them from being washed away by floodwaters. In Hankou, the water level rose to 32.5 feet last month, but then gradually receded, easing people's fears. However, it rose more than 3 feet overnight on the 26th, exceeding 35 feet 5 inches yesterday. The highest level reached 38 feet. Fortunately, the Wutai sluice gate was built early and is solid, preventing a breach. However, if it rises further, it will still be dangerous. Yesterday, the local Flood Relief Committee held an emergency meeting to discuss disaster relief and response measures.

Transportation Disrupted: Due to continuous flooding, several ports in Hunan and Ganzhou have been submerged. Yesterday, local shipping companies received telegrams from Hunan and Ganzhou stating that goods being shipped to Changsha, Yiyang, Changde, and other places in Hunan have been halted due to floodwaters. Goods being shipped to the interior of Ganzhou Province have also been temporarily suspended due to the Nanzun road being blocked by floodwaters. As a result, exports from Shanghai to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River have been greatly reduced.

The National Government Flood Relief Committee to Conclude on July 1st 156

Concluding Committee to be Organized and Staffed to Preside; Unfinished Matters to Continue Until Completion

The National Government Flood Relief Committee, which held a standing committee meeting on the 18th of this month, proposed to begin the winding down of various departments and agencies from July 1st of this year. However, unfinished work would continue. The proposal was passed, and the committee chairman, Mr. T.V. Soong, convened a plenary session of the committee at the Central Bank Finance Department office at 2:30 PM yesterday to decide that the committee would begin its conclusion from July 1st. However, all unfinished matters would still be handled responsibly. The meeting adjourned at 5:30 PM. Details are as follows:

Attendees Yesterday The attendees at yesterday's meeting included Committee Chairman T.V. Soong, committee members Zhang Shouyong, Liu Ruiheng, Wang Xiao, Shi Liangcai, Baker, Zheng Lai, Zhu Ziqiao, Xu Shiying, Wang Yiting, Zhang Gongquan, Wei Wenbin, Xi Dejiong, Zha Liangzhao, Anders, Lin Kanghou, Guo Dehua, and more than fifty others.

Chairman Soong's Address National Government Flood Relief Committee Chairman Soong delivered the opening remarks, stating: "Esteemed committee members, the initial work report of this committee since its establishment has been compiled and is now available for your reference. The resolution of the Standing Committee on June 18th is also submitted today for your discussion. You will recall that at the first general meeting of this committee on September 9th last year, I stated that the scale of this flood was unprecedented in history. It might be possible to alleviate it slightly, but it would be impossible to completely avoid it. At that time, I also said that the way to provide relief should be through the joint efforts of public and private sectors. However, in any case, funds are limited, so the use of funds should be very careful. It is better to choose the main work and focus on it to achieve the greatest effect, and do not overextend, resulting in diminishing returns. At that time, the committee decided on the following measures: the first step was emergency relief work, to provide as much relief as possible to the people in the disaster area, providing clothing, food, housing, and sanitation. The second step was, after the flood receded, to repair the embankments that were washed away by the flood as far as financial resources allowed, and to increase their height and solidity to prevent future flooding of the Yangtze River under normal water flow. The final work was to save money to help with spring plowing and post-disaster farmland reconstruction. The most important of these tasks is embankment construction. With the completion of the embankments, emergency relief funds will not be wasted, and post-disaster farmland reconstruction will also be easier. The opinion of the Standing Committee is that the main work within the committee's economic capacity has been 90% successful according to the original plan. Unfinished work has also been planned and can be carried out step by step, so there was the resolution of June 18th. The amount of work of this committee depends on the financial situation. When the committee was first established, in addition to private donations, some people in the community believed that the government should issue 80 million yuan in disaster relief bonds to purchase wheat from the three northeastern provinces for disaster relief. However, the persons in charge of this committee all believed that the market was sluggish and there was no power to absorb this huge amount of bonds. The yield of wheat in the eastern provinces depended on transportation, weather, personnel, and other factors, so its effectiveness could not be guaranteed. Therefore, after many discussions, it was decided to adopt the following methods: (1) Purchase surplus wheat from the United States on credit with long-term payments; (2) Raise private donations; (3) Impose a surtax on customs duties. After the above methods were decided, they were implemented one by one. The facts of the past few months are enough to prove that the committee's methods were correct. On September 25th last year, the National Government officially signed an agreement with the U.S. government to purchase 15 million bushels of American wheat and flour on credit, valued at US$9,212,828.46, which is approximately 43,000,000 yuan in national currency at the current exchange rate. This debt will be repaid with a 5% ad valorem surtax, which will be levied from August 1st of this year until it is paid off. Private donations have reached 7,387,400 yuan in national currency since the fundraising began. There are many voluntary disaster relief organizations established by private individuals in various parts of the country, which have absorbed a large amount of donations. In addition, the world economy is depressed, and the violent Japanese have repeatedly invaded our territory, first attacking the eastern provinces and then committing crimes in Shanghai. All of these factors have affected fundraising, but it is gratifying that this achievement has been made. Due to the sluggish market for government bonds, it was decided to withdraw the proposed 30 million yuan in disaster relief bonds and instead levy a 10% surtax on customs duties for a period of eight months, from December 1st last year to July 31st this year. From the beginning of the levy to June 20th, the income from this surtax has reached 12,131,555 yuan in national currency. The budget set by the committee at the first general meeting in September last year was 70,000,000 yuan in national currency, and the committee's income from public and private donations, including American wheat, is approximately 65,000,000 yuan in national currency, so the difference between the budget and the actual number is not much. On the expenditure side of the committee, one-third of the American wheat was used for emergency relief, agricultural relief, and subsidies for the repair of private embankments, and the remaining two-thirds were used for embankment construction wages. Other expenses were also not much different from the budget resolved in the general meeting in September last year. Transportation costs were slightly lower than the budget. In addition, there were many places in the disaster area where transportation was difficult, so some of the wheat was exchanged for cash to facilitate convenience. The flood last year was unprecedented in history, so there was no precedent for this kind of huge relief work. The staff were also temporarily recruited from various parts of the country. Among them were engineers, accountants, and doctors from public and private institutions, students from various schools who could serve as surveyors and investigators, missionaries with rich disaster relief experience and familiarity with local conditions, and grain depot staff temporarily hired. Mistakes in the work were inevitable. However, the committee dares to assert that even if there are mistakes in the work, they are mostly due to lack of experience and not due to errors of conscience. What is most noteworthy is that the expenditure of 65,000,000 yuan was not involved in political influence, nor was it subject to political interference or control. This is also something that the committee can be proud of. The fact that the work has been intense and unremitting from beginning to end is even more important. Even when the violent Japanese were invading and the gunfire was continuous, and in the communist areas where there was a risk of attack, the staff were still able to carry out the relief work as usual, and it was not heard that it was suspended due to fear or difficulty. The staff of this committee proceeded with this spirit and continued unremittingly, so that they were able to build a dam of 5,000 kilometers in this short period of time (along the Yangtze River from Shashi to Guazhou below Zhenjiang, and along the Han River, Huai River, and Grand Canal where there is a risk of flooding). Most of this huge project was newly built, and the number of workers employed reached 1.4 million at its peak. From now on, even if the Yangtze River overflows, unless it exceeds the ordinary, it should not cause a major disaster again. All the staff of the committee (most of whom are unpaid) are admirable for their loyalty and integrity in handling affairs. Outstanding among them are Sir Simpson and General Zhu Qinglan. These two gentlemen are enthusiastic, fair, diligent day and night. The success of this committee is largely due to the efforts of these two gentlemen. Regarding the proposal made by the Standing Committee, I have a word to explain it. 90% of the work planned by this committee has been completed, and this huge organization is no longer needed. The unfinished projects have been planned, funds have been prepared, and they can be carried out step by step to completion. According to the above situation, the committee believes that the committee's affairs can now begin to be wound down so that the progress can be reported to the government as soon as possible. The permanent maintenance of the dike in the future should also be proposed to the government for selection and completion of the task.

Report on Disaster Area Work Next, the Disaster Area Work Group of the Flood Relief Committee reported on the progress since its establishment: (1) After the establishment of the association in August 20, it began relief efforts and requested Colonel and Mrs. Lindbergh of the United States to assist in measuring the disaster situation in Anhui and Jiangsu, and British naval aviation experts to assist in measuring the Hebei area, and produced a disaster area map of the Yangtze River and Huai River basin. (2) The process of contacting the United States to purchase US wheat on credit, as well as the exact number distributed to various disaster areas. (3) The establishment of the Industrial Relief Office, specially requesting the Yangtze River, Huai River, tributaries, and Grand Canal main dikes, as well as the river diversion projects into the sea in Jiangbei near the sea. (4) The exact number of voluntary relief funds distributed to various disaster areas. (5) The situation of accommodating more than 500,000 refugees during the worst disaster and the total number of porridge factories established. (6) The process of handling agricultural relief. (7) The situation of transporting American wheat, as well as the process of selling a part of the American wheat for cash. (8) Results of inspections and audits of accounts in various places. (9) The organization and diagnosis situation of the epidemic prevention office. (10) Detailed report on the association's financial revenue and expenditure.

Resolving to Conclude Various Cases After the Disaster Area Work Group completed its report, the committee members present successively expressed their opinions. Everyone had no objection to the conclusion of the committee, so they began to discuss the proposals. (1) Resolved that the committee will begin to conclude the various departments and agencies from July 1st of this year, but unfinished work will continue. (2) Resolved that all work that should continue will be wound up successively after completion. (3) Resolved that the chairman will select several members of the committee to form a concluding committee to handle all affairs. Zeng Rongfu, Wei Wenbin, Baker, Xi Dejiong, Zha Liangzhao, Anders, and other six people were appointed as concluding committee members to be responsible for presiding over the concluding affairs of the association.

Carrying out Unfinished Matters Although the association has decided to begin to conclude from July 1st of this year, all unfinished projects should still be carried out according to the original plan. Currently, the work that the association has not yet completed is the completion of the embankment, as well as the inspection and maintenance of the summer embankment, the sorting and auditing of accounts. Due to the scale of the project and the complexity of the accounts, it will take at least three or four months to complete all of them. However, the handling of the concluding matters should be jointly handled by the concluding committee and the accounting and auditing personnel. It is hoped that the accounting books can be cleared by the end of October or early November, and the auditors will prove that there are no errors. At that time, all the tasks of the association can be completely completed.

Workers of the Ordnance Factory Petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday 158

And also went to the Garrison Headquarters

Petition to the Municipal Party Headquarters Again Today

The plan to shut down the Shanghai Ordnance Factory, after the factory sent representatives to Nanjing to request a resumption of work, has now been temporarily suspended. However, the future of the shutdown is still pending. The Ministry of Military Administration has not yet made a decision and must wait for a telegram from Chairman Chiang Kai-shek before there can be a clear expression. On the workers' side, at 10 AM yesterday morning, representatives Mei Jixin, Yuan Genquan, Chen Yaohua, Zhang Houfu, Lu Shengquan, Chen Changzhou, Sun Songming, Ji Zhiping, and other eight people were dispatched to the Municipal Government to petition first. They went to see Mayor Wu Tiecheng. Because Wu was very busy meeting guests, he sent staff member Wang to receive them on his behalf. The workers informed Wang about the purpose of the petition and presented a petition document. The document contained four points explaining the reasons for requesting a resumption of work: (1) Many of the provisions of the Bromley's recommendations are not appropriate. (2) Many of the Shanghai factory's machinery parts have rusted severely while abroad. If there is a delay, they will become waste. (3) The Shanghai factory is a shield for the southeastern half of the country and has repeatedly made miraculous achievements. It should not be shut down, which would affect national defense. (4) The workers of the Shanghai factory manufactured weapons for the 19th Route Army during the anti-Japanese war, which had an indirect effect. Their livelihoods should be maintained and the factory should not be shut down. The eight representatives requested that Wang relay this intention to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek of the Military Affairs Commission. Wang promised to ask Mayor Wu to fulfill this request. Later, the representatives went to the Garrison Headquarters to see Commander Dai. Because Dai was not there, Adjutant Zheng Youshang met with them on his behalf. He expressed his deep sympathy for the representatives' requests and promised to relay them to Commander Dai and send a telegram to Chairman Chiang Kai-shek to continue handling the matter. The workers' representatives then withdrew and planned to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters again this morning.

Nisshin's Tangshan Maru Crashed into Chinese Ship Haiping 160

Crashed into 裏 Tongsha

Returned to Shanghai for Repairs Yesterday

The Shanghai Yingkou liner Haiping of the Shanghai Haichang Company was sailing from Shanghai to Niuzhuang when it was hit by the North Ocean liner Tangshan Maru of the Nisshin Company outside the Wusong estuary near the 裏 Tongsha lightship (about 60 nautical miles from Shanghai), causing considerable damage. The responsibility for the accident lies entirely with the Japanese ship. The reporter has investigated the details of the incident and recorded them as follows:

The Truth of the Accident The Haiping was loaded with cargo and passengers in Shanghai and set off for Yingkou at 4 PM on the 25th. At 8:28 PM that night, when it approached the 裏 Tongsha lightship, the Haiping's navigator was steering southeast by two and a half points south, following the navigation ship. Suddenly, a ship came from the opposite direction, first seeing a green light. At 8:30 PM, another ship was seen, showing a red light. The Haiping then changed course to southeast east by one-quarter east S·EIE1/4E. The ship showing the green light sounded its whistle once. The ships showing the red light followed one after another, heading forward. In order to avoid the accident, the Haiping steered towards the side of the Jiuduan lightship and sounded its whistle twice. At that time, one ship had already passed, and the ship showing the red light was the Tangshan Maru of the Nisshin Company, which was traveling from Tianjin to Shanghai via Qingdao. At this time, it also answered twice, indicating that it was passing on the right side. The Haiping then made way to the left. At 8:40 PM, the Tangshan Maru showed a red light. Unexpectedly, one minute later, the Tangshan Maru showed both red and green lights, indicating that its hull was heading towards the Haiping. At this time, the left side of the Haiping was close to the lightship, and there was no room to make way. In an instant, the bow of the Tangshan Maru crashed into the starboard side of the Haiping.

Damage The Haiping had no way to retreat at that time, but the bow of the Tangshan Maru did not deviate to the right but turned to the left, resulting in the collision. The starboard side of the third cargo hold of the Haiping was hit hard by the bow of the Tangshan Maru, and the iron plates were completely destroyed, creating a large hole. Fortunately, the place that was hit was still above the waterline, so although the seawater rushed in violently, it did not immediately sink. If it had been damaged below the waterline, it would have sunk to the bottom of the sea long ago. There was a lot of cargo in the third hold, which was all soaked by the water that rushed in, causing considerable damage. The bow of the Tangshan Maru was also damaged. After causing the accident, the ship ignored everything and sailed to Shanghai.

Grounding Itself After the Haiping was hit, it was deeply afraid that the heavy load and water intake would be unsustainable, or that an accident would occur. Therefore, within 20 minutes of being hit, the shipowner himself drove the Haiping to the shallow beach near the lightship to run aground to avoid accidents and to show seriousness. The shipowner tried to pump out some of the accumulated water from the third hold and reported to Shanghai that the damage was too severe to travel long distances. It was not until yesterday morning that the Haiping was driven out of the shallows at high tide and returned to Shanghai to carry out inspections and repairs and negotiate with the Japanese merchants.

Returned to Shanghai for Repairs The Haiping returned to Shanghai from the 裏 Tongsha Jiuduan lightship yesterday and was docked at the 25th and 26th river cylinders inside the Yongkou. The shipowner reported to the company and the customs, and first sent personnel to the ship to inspect the damaged areas and planned to unload the cargo from the third hold, and then repair the hole. Passengers on board had to go ashore and take other ships. They negotiated with Nisshin on the other hand. The amount of loss has not yet been determined, but the damage to both ships and cargo is considerable. The ship is 2,360 tons and was built in 1897.

Hongkou Silk Factories Completely Shut Down Yesterday 162

Party and Government Agencies Sent Personnel to Thoroughly Investigate and Mediate

The Guild Will Hold a Meeting Tomorrow to Discuss Solutions

Following the strike by workers at the Yichang and other silk factories in Hongkou, the situation has become serious, and the strike is spreading. Of the ten single-reeling silk factories that were operating, eight have joined the strike, and two have voluntarily announced a shutdown. Party and government agencies dispatched personnel yesterday to seek mediation. The trade association is scheduled to hold a meeting tomorrow to discuss solutions. The details are as follows:

Strike Increases: Following the strike by workers at Yichang Silk Factory, workers at five other factories, including Xiangcheng, Yuncheng, Tongwei, Yujing, and Xinlun, were also dissuaded from working and joined the strike. The night before last, all workers at the 208 silk reeling machines at Houfu Silk Factory on Zhangjiaxiang Road and the 208 silk reeling machines at Weiyu Silk Factory also joined the strike. As of yesterday morning, a total of eight factories, with more than 5,000 male and female workers, had joined the strike. The factory authorities automatically suspended operations at 352 silk reeling machines at Renji Silk Factory on Tiantong Road and 312 silk reeling machines at Tongyi Silk Factory on Zhangjiaxiang Road. As a result, the single-reeling silk factories in the Hongkou district are completely shut down. Only the 224 silk reeling machines at the Fulunheng double-reeling factory are unaffected because they have no connection with the single-reeling factories.

Guild's Response: At 8:00 AM yesterday, all directors of the Fourth District Silk Reeling Industry Union held an informal meeting to discuss solutions. They originally planned to send Chen Xiufu, Le Xiaorong, and others to negotiate with Shen, the chairman of the trade association. However, after receiving the guild's response, they stopped their trip. The original letter is recorded below: To the respondents, regarding your letters of the 22nd and 24th of this month, and the statements made by your representatives, we have understood everything. We are now sending letters to all silk factories to pay close attention to working hours and careful production. As for the issue of wages, we will convene a meeting of the industry next week to discuss and decide, and then inform you. We are writing to inform you in advance. Please take note. Sincerely, Fourth District Silk Reeling Industry Union.

Party and Government Investigation: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, considering that the silk factory workers' strike concerns local security, specially dispatched Zhu Guilin, together with Zhou Lianze of the Municipal Party Headquarters, at 1:00 PM yesterday to thoroughly investigate the strike with both labor and management, in order to mediate and avoid the expansion of the labor unrest. At the same time, Wu Tingxun, the chief of the Fifth District Third Sub-Bureau of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, was ordered to dispatch armed police officers to station in various silk factories within the district to provide protection and strictly prevent thugs from infiltrating and inciting labor unrest. The strike situation has already been reported to the General Bureau for review and handling.

Management Meeting: The Shanghai Silk Factory Trade Association is scheduled to convene a general meeting of all members on the 29th of this month (i.e., tomorrow, Wednesday) to discuss the labor unrest issue.

Sixth District Requests: Of the silk factories operating in the Zhabei district, there are a total of 14, including Ruifengyu, Gongji, Lunchang, and Yuanfeng. The Sixth District Silk Reeling Industry Union, believing that the wage issue concerns all silk factories in the city and fearing its spread and the occurrence of unfortunate events, yesterday morning separately advised workers at each factory to wait patiently for party and government agencies to mediate according to the law and not to act without authorization. Fortunately, all workers deeply understood the greater good and decided to wait patiently for the union to negotiate. At 2:00 PM, they sent representatives Wu Suzhen, Yang Gengdi, and others to negotiate with the trade association. Chairman Shen promised to provide a satisfactory response after the meeting.

Brewing Labor Unrest in the National Pharmaceutical Industry 163

A Strike is About to Happen.

The situation between labor and management in the local national pharmaceutical industry is worsening. At a time when the epidemic is spreading, a strike would hit patients the hardest. It is hoped that both sides can show mutual concession and seek a reasonable solution. This would be a blessing for society and not just for the industry itself. The details are summarized as follows:

News from the Pharmaceutical Workers' Union 164

The labor unrest in the local national pharmaceutical industry is becoming more serious as employers refuse workers' demands, and a strike is likely to occur. The local party and government agencies have reached an agreement on how to handle the situation. The details are as follows:

Workers' Meeting: Yesterday at 2:00 PM, the wage increase campaign committee held its first meeting. Chairman Feng Xingkang resolved the following matters: (1) The resolution of the executive meeting of the wage increase campaign committee was discussed and passed. (2) The wage increase campaign committee should elect a five-member chairman group. Zhao Zhenhui, Fang Qingjian, Yuan Pinzhang, Chen Yuantao, and Feng Xingkang were elected. (3) Future declarations and interviews with reporters should be based on the resolution. The resolution was passed. (4) The committee should contact the trade association about the wage increase issue. Should a date and number of people be determined? It was resolved that the number of people would be seven. In addition to the original chairman group, Zhu Xiaqing and Fang Qinghe were elected as representatives. The date was set for 1:00 PM on the 28th, gathering at the second district branch. (5) A notice to all district branches to strengthen grassroots work was passed. (6) The resignation requests of comrades Zhao Zhenhui and Han Bingyao were discussed. It was resolved to unanimously retain them.

Document to the Party Headquarters: A document was submitted stating that the National Pharmaceutical Trade Association is instructing its members to undermine labor-management conditions separately, requesting instructions to stop this in order to eliminate disputes and benefit the labor movement. The union held a general meeting of all employee representatives on the afternoon of the 24th of this month, and it was reported that representatives had been sent to guide the meeting. Now, the resolutions and requirements are recorded and submitted to the committee: (1) The employers of Qintongde, Fengcunren, Yetian de, and other three stores have violated the conditions and refused to hire substitutes. (2) The employer of Wangyuandao hires non-union members, causing increased unemployment and extending working hours. (3) Shouquanzhai and Hongji and other stores oppress employees and extend working hours. (4) Recently, the trade association used coercive methods to deceive employees in the outer sections to join the association, dividing the union's organization. The outer sections' employees unanimously swore to oppose this. It is humbly requested that the National Pharmaceutical Trade Association be instructed to accept and implement these measures to eliminate disputes and benefit the labor movement. This would be a great favor. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee.

Refuting the Employers: The Pharmaceutical Workers' Union, in response to the report in the newspaper about Zhang Meian of the Pharmaceutical Trade Association's statement on the dispute, stated that many of the points were untrue. Yesterday, they specially wrote a rebuttal as follows: (1) Regarding the labor-management contract, Mr. Zhang believes it was illegally privately signed. It should be known that the labor-management contract was signed by the five parties of the government, military, and labor following legal procedures. How can it be said to be illegal? Moreover, the contract is permanently valid, and neither party can violate it. Now, employers such as Caitongde and Fengcunren have refused to hire substitutes, while Wangyuandao and other stores have hired non-members without authorization, and Shouquanzhai and other stores have extended working hours, which is obviously a deliberate breach of contract. (2) The issue of outer-section employees. The nature of pharmaceutical work is different from other industries. Ordinary pharmacies are both internal and external, and most can be considered technical. Therefore, employees must not only serve customers and sell goods but also perform other technical work. The major pharmacies in this city have had to divide into inner and outer sections due to the development of their business. In fact, both inner and outer sections are workers and are equal. As for the interpretation of the former Central Training Department and the Ministry of Industry, it is feared that they did not understand the actual situation of the pharmaceutical industry at that time or were deceived by the employers. (3) Legal issues. Since the promulgation of the Trade Union Law, after the cancellation of employee organizations, the central government and the local party and government agencies have announced that the original labor-management contracts remain valid. The union's maintenance of the original contract is a legitimate action in compliance with the law. (4) The issue of employees joining the trade association. The employers consider outer-section employees to be clerks and force them to join the trade association. It should be known that even if employees are considered clerks, they have the freedom to join the trade association. How can they be forced? Moreover, it is questionable whether joining is beneficial to employees. (5) The issue of dispatching substitutes. The right to dispatch substitutes is in the hands of the labor party, as clearly stipulated in the contract. The employers cannot refuse it. (6) The issue of wage increases. The wage rate of employees in this industry is extremely low. Although there have been several negotiations for wage increases, the monthly salary of each person is still only 16 yuan. In this period of high living costs, this meager salary is not enough to make ends meet. Moreover, the employers have repeatedly increased retail prices. After the Shanghai war, business has been better than before. Therefore, workers' demand for wage increases is justified. (7) The issue of placing the unemployed. The number of people in the pharmaceutical industry increases every year due to the apprenticeship system. As a result, many are unemployed. It is necessary to find ways to place them, which would affect their livelihoods. However, the employers do not care and refuse to hire unemployed members as substitutes, and even dismiss working employees. Their intentions are obvious.

The Authorities' Handling: A reporter from the Dagong newspaper visited Xu Shifu, the chief of the third section of the Social Affairs Bureau, yesterday to inquire about the authorities' handling of the labor unrest. He replied that the bureau had sent staff to attend and guide the meeting when the union convened a meeting of members the other day. According to the staff's report, the atmosphere at the meeting was extremely tense, and a strike was feared. The bureau believes that if the pharmaceutical industry goes on strike during this summer season of epidemic prevention, it will have a major impact on the lives of patients and the public health of society. Therefore, it attaches great importance to this issue. However, the labor unrest arose from the employer's breach of the labor-management contract signed in 1927. The crux of the matter lies in whether the contract remains valid due to changes in laws and regulations. Once this issue is resolved, other issues can be easily solved. Therefore, the bureau has sent a letter to the municipal party headquarters to handle the matter properly and has scheduled a meeting to discuss handling the situation. It has also ordered both sides of the industry to submit the agreed conditions to the bureau for review in order to study them and has ordered the labor side to wait patiently for a resolution and not to take immediate action, in order to eliminate the dispute invisibly and protect public safety.

News from the Trade Association 165

The National Pharmaceutical Trade Association convened an emergency executive committee meeting yesterday to discuss how to deal with the labor unrest. In addition to all the executive committee members, more than 200 trade members attended and participated. Zhuang Meitang was elected chairman, and it was resolved to reject the union's demands and issue a declaration to the public. At the same time, several representatives were sent to the competent authorities to petition and stop the union's overstepping actions. The details are as follows:

Key Resolutions: (1) On the issue of demarcating the boundaries between inner and outer section employees in this industry, the association is executing orders and it is difficult to change according to the law. Therefore, the association will not interfere with the union's opposition to the demarcation. (2) The association is following the Social Affairs Bureau's instructions in refusing substitutes from the outer sections. All unemployed clerks should register with the association. The association will introduce them to various stores as substitutes at any time. It is difficult to accept the union's unauthorized appointment. (3) The association firmly opposes the union's demand for a wage increase of 10 yuan per person per month. (4) Cen Zhiliang, Zhang Meian, Zhou Qiansheng, and Feng Jinpu were elected as representatives to petition various authorities for relief. (5) A declaration will be issued to the public. (6) A general meeting of members will be convened in advance in order to deal with the situation uniformly. (7) Pharmaceutical employees are advised not to be used and endanger society. All members are notified to deal with the environment with a calm and composed spirit. (8) If necessary, the association will set up temporary pharmacies in various places together with the medical community to facilitate patients' purchase of medicine.

Declaration:

We, the pharmaceutical employers, have long been the meat on the chopping block of the drug workers, and are now about to suffer the unjust accusations and oppression of a workers' strike. The reasons the pharmaceutical workers are using to justify their strike this time are: first, that the employers have violated the labor-management conditions; second, that they are upholding the substitute worker system; and third, that they are demanding wage increases. But the revision of the labor-management conditions in our industry is an order from the central government; the improvement of the substitute worker system is an instruction from the Social Affairs Bureau; what fault is it of us employers? As for increasing wages, we employers have already increased them again and again, making them the highest in the national pharmaceutical industry. At a time when the great war has just ended and the social economy is bankrupt, the employers are seeking life but cannot, seeking death but cannot, and the affectionate workers want to demand wage increases at this time; are they not harboring ulterior motives? Among the pharmaceutical workers in the city, there must be many who are aware of the current situation; they should know that today's government and laws are all complete and clear, not like the lawless and reckless bandits who roamed Shanghai during the 16th year of the Republic. All citizens of our country have the obligation to abide by the law. If the pharmaceutical workers still know the meaning of the word "national law," then all their actions should be based on the law. If they rely on the crowd, coerce, and hope to gain an advantage by chance, I fear they will inevitably be subject to legal sanctions. Moreover, the current society is not one where one hand can cover the sky and deceive oneself. Even if we employers can be coerced and subdued by the workers, the people of society all have (eyes), and public opinion is inescapable. Speaking of the present, the treatment and living conditions of pharmaceutical workers in Shanghai, although not as good as those of the general public, are not subject to management and have the freedom to enter and exit, which is still better than them. The cause of this labor unrest is due to a few troublemakers in the union who are using it to seek personal gain, not hesitating to stir up trouble and spread rumors to create a terrifying situation. Their conspiracies and schemes are deeply rooted. How can the pharmaceutical workers of the city be willing to be used and not know to return? The only ones who are indirectly harmed are the patients in society. Therefore, those in society who have the ability to judge and adjudicate should not ignore this pharmaceutical labor unrest and should quickly rise up and make righteous claims, so that the unfortunate situation can be eliminated invisibly. We employers will abide by the law until death, and we hope for your wise consideration.

Orders from the Ministry and Approvals from the Bureau:

The Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang issued Order No. 290:

It is hereby ordered that the facts are known. According to the letter No. 17513 from the Central Training Department, "According to the report submitted by your committee's former People's Training Committee on the service situation of the workers in the duck and pharmaceutical industries, please review," it has been received by the Ministry. While it is under review, a letter from the Ministry of Industry also stated, "The personnel working in the pill and powder and decoction departments of the pharmaceutical industry also take care of both inner and outer court work. It should be determined based on their main work. If the personnel in the two departments also take care of the outer court work, then they should join the trade union. If they also take care of the inner court work after the outer court work, then they should join the trade association," etc. After checking, the nature of the service of the employers in the duck industry is roughly the same as the personnel in the pill and powder and decoction departments of the pharmaceutical industry who also take care of the inner and outer court work. Their organizations can refer to the above explanation and join the trade union or trade association separately. As requested in the previous report, it is hereby replied to you. In addition to issuing separate orders, it is hereby informed. This order.

Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau Order No. 1911:

Received the report. After checking, clerks cannot join the trade union according to law, and the trade union cannot overstep its authority to dispatch. From now on, when there are unemployed clerks, they should register with the trade association so that they can be introduced, which is in accordance with laws and regulations. In addition to approving the instructions to the trade union to proceed accordingly, it is hereby notified. This approval.

Document to the Municipal Government:

The document is submitted stating that pharmaceutical workers are illegally coercing and brewing a strike. Please strictly stop them to protect the people's health. This association has been reading in the newspapers for days that the Shanghai Pharmaceutical Trade Union convened a meeting of members' representatives regarding cases where the employers refused to hire substitutes, demarcated the boundaries between inner and outer section clerks, and demanded a wage increase of 10 yuan per person per month, and resolved to prepare for a strike to deal with it, etc. Reading it, I am extremely horrified. After checking, the association is acting in accordance with the orders of the Ministry of Industry and the Central Training Department to demarcate the boundaries between inner and outer section clerks in the pharmaceutical industry. The association is following the instructions of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to refuse the trade union's unauthorized dispatch of substitutes in the outer section. As for the request for a wage increase, this association cannot accept it at a time when the great war has just ended and commerce is declining. However, the trade union is disregarding the people's health and planning a strike to coerce, which is extremely illegal. It is reasonable to prepare a document and submit it to the municipal government, humbly requesting that the government strictly order them to stop it, in order to prevent disputes and maintain the people's health. This would be greatly appreciated. Respectfully submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Government.

The Taxpayers Association Asks the Municipal Council Not to Collect Extra-Settlement House Taxes 166

The Chinese Taxpayers Association of the Public Concession yesterday sent a letter to the General Office of the Municipal Council, saying:

Dear Sir,

According to the letter from Dai Chunlin of Caojiadu on June 24, during the Shanghai war, he rented a house at No. 14 Sanyi Lane, by the extra-settlement road on Jessfield Road. He has already moved out for four months. At first, a Chinese tax collector from the Public Concession, speaking with a Suzhou accent, went to collect 18 taels of silver for the spring tax for Sanyi Lane. Because the area belongs to the Chinese territory and is not equipped with concession electric lights or telephones, he politely refused. At the end of April, the council sent a notice of spring tax due for Sanyi Lane, totaling 12 taels of silver, and a notice of summer tax due, totaling 18 taels of silver. This morning (June 24), the tax collector came again to collect the tax and said that he had to pay the summer tax together with the two seasons' taxes for Sanyi Lane, otherwise he would add the tax. After a while, he borrowed a Westerner to come, and he answered with the same words. The Westerner, through an interpreter, said that if it was not paid this morning, he would come in the afternoon to cut the electric light wires and seal the door.

According to the letter from Renfengzhai on June 24, during the Shanghai war, several friends sought refuge, and a small number of people temporarily borrowed a house at No. 11 Sanyi Lane, near the extra-settlement road on Jessfield Road. Around early April, the Chinese tax collector of the Municipal Council came to the small store and wanted to collect 18 taels of silver for the spring tax for Sanyi Lane. He replied that the place was beside the extra-settlement road and was not equipped with concession telephones or electric lights, so he should not pay. He also said that the place had already been moved out. The tax collector said that it could be changed to 12 taels of silver. At the end of April, the tax office sent two notices, one for the spring tax of 12 taels and the other for the summer tax of 18 taels. This morning, the Chinese came to the small store to collect the summer tax, and they paid the full amount of tax they should pay. After a while, the tax collector who wanted to collect the tax for Sanyi Lane came with a Westerner and wanted to collect 12 taels of silver for the spring tax for No. 11 Sanyi Lane. He replied as before.

It is beyond doubt that the house tax beside the extra-settlement road should be collected by the Shanghai Municipal Government. Moreover, it should not cause further complications or misunderstandings while the problem is being resolved. According to the letter above, we request that your council, according to law, prevent the tax collectors' extra-legal actions.

Sincerely,

Shanghai Public Concession Chinese Taxpayers Association

Pudong Electric Company Supplies Hengda Yarn Factory with Electricity 167

Hengda New Kee Yarn Factory in Yangsi Bridge, Pudong, is a large-scale factory. Manager Chen Zisheng has been carefully planning, so the business has been booming in recent years. It is quite developed. It has a 500-kilowatt steam turbine generator to supply the factory's electricity needs. However, it consumes a lot of coal and is very uneconomical. It often needs to be shut down for repairs, which hinders work and causes huge hidden losses. It has now reached a satisfactory agreement with the Pudong Electric Company to switch to electricity supplied by the company. It is said that the contracted electricity price is quite low, which can save a lot of expenses every month. Moreover, the company has a sufficient amount of electricity, which can be expanded at any time, and the continuous supply throughout the year will prevent work from being interrupted, which is especially convenient.

Sniping of a Beautiful Young Woman 168

Shot Five Times, Life in Critical Danger

The Reason for the Attack is Difficult to Guess

At 10:35 last night, a young woman on the third floor of Dechang Foreign Goods Store, No. 118, Former New Street, near the Grand Clock Tower in the French Concession, was suddenly assassinated by a gunman. She was shot five times all over her body and her life is in critical danger. The murderer escaped from the scene. The details are described below:

Beautiful Young Woman: Song Jinfeng, a woman from Pudong, is 26 years old, slender and beautiful. A year ago, she became acquainted with Zhou Yongkang (nicknamed "Little Baldy"), a well-known gangster, and rented a house together at No. 118, Former New Street, Maidian Road, French Concession, on the fourth floor of Dechang Foreign Goods Cloth Store, the back door is No. 31, Mingde Lane.

Smoking Opium: Little Baldy Zhou Yongkang usually makes a living by gambling. Since the outbreak of the Shanghai war, he has been in financial straits. He leaves early and returns late every day, borrowing money to make a living. At about 10:30 last night, Zhou was not yet home, and Jinfeng went to the Yanzi Nest opened by a local old woman on the third floor to smoke opium for fun. Before she could go to bed, a violent guest suddenly arrived.

Five Shots Sniped: Jinfeng had just entered the old woman's room and was sitting on a round stool chatting, waiting for another person to finish smoking. Before she could say a few words, two people wearing blue short outfits suddenly rushed up from downstairs. One person leaned against the side of the door, poked his head inside, and the other person took out a pistol and aimed five shots at Jinfeng. The bullets pierced through her like a string of pearls.

Falling in Response: At the sound of the gunshots, Jinfeng fell in response. Everyone in the room was pale and frozen like wooden chickens. The murderer took the opportunity to escape. The old woman immediately ran to the Grand Clock Tower police station to report. The head of the police immediately sent detectives to investigate. They found that Jinfeng had been shot five times all over her body, including two shots in the chest, one shot in each of her left and right hands, and one shot in the abdomen.

Life in Critical Danger: After the police finished investigating, they immediately transported Jinfeng to Renji Hospital. Due to excessive blood loss, she was unconscious upon arrival at the hospital. Her life is in critical danger. Soon after, Zhou Yongkang heard the news and rushed to the scene. He immediately reported to Song Guisheng, Jinfeng's father, who runs a Tiger Dumpling Stove on Renzhi Lane, North Sichuan Road. According to the speculation of the general public, Song's encounter with violence may contain an affair, or it may be Little Baldy's enemies who came to assassinate Little Baldy. Because he was not at home, Jinfeng was mistakenly targeted.

Zhao's Disciple Denies "Old Man"

Ye Shantao Cannot Shirk Responsibility as Director 170

Second Branch of the High Court Pronounces Judgment Yesterday

Ye Sentenced to Imprisonment for Forgery

Zhou Songqing and Others Mutually Acknowledge Being Directors

Escrow Dispute Still Developing

Second Branch of the High Court's Judgment: After Huang Chu'jiu's death, the various businesses operated by his Gongfa Company, such as the Riyue Bank, the Dashijie Amusement Savings Department, and other financial institutions, successively collapsed, greatly affecting depositors. Because Gongfa was not a limited liability company, the shareholders and directors should bear unlimited liability. Therefore, the creditor groups pursued them. Ye Shantao, a wealthy businessman from Haiyan living in Shanghai, was also one of Gongfa's directors. When the creditors negotiated with him, he presented a letter signed by Huang Chu'jiu, stating that he had resigned as a director and had long disassociated himself from Gongfa. However, the creditors all believed that the letter was forged and jointly sued Ye for forgery. After the First Special District Local Court concluded its trial, it acquitted Ye Shantao on the grounds that the plaintiff's evidence was insufficient. After this setback, Zhang Zhengji and Zhu Chengfei expressed reluctance to continue the proceedings. Only Dong Longxing and Chen Kaifu's lawyer, Yan Luqing, still filed an appeal, requesting the reversal of the original judgment and further investigation. Hundreds of depositors of the Riyue Bank and the Amusement Savings Department recently sent a special letter to lawyer Yan, praising him for fighting for the interests of poor creditors. The Second Branch of the High Court also believed that the official case concerned the interests of the creditors and should not be hastily concluded. It held several hearings and conducted secret deliberations. Only yesterday afternoon did the Second Branch of the High Court's Criminal First Tribunal, presided over by Judge Yu, together with Judges Jiang and Zhao, specially convene a joint court to announce the judgment. The main text read: "The original judgment is reversed. Ye Shantao is sentenced to three months imprisonment with a two-year reprieve for forgery. The forged letter from Huang Chu'jiu is confiscated." However, Ye was not present when the judgment was announced, so it is still unknown whether he will accept the judgment.

Third Branch of the High Court Continues Trial: In the case of the collapse of the Shanghai Riyue Bank and the Dashijie Amusement Savings Department, the former French Concession court ruled that Zhao Qinbo, Zhou Songqing, and others should bear the responsibility of shareholders and directors of Gongfa Company, and dismissed the part concerning Ye Shantao. Subsequently, because the creditors were dissatisfied, they hired a lawyer to file an appeal in the Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, requesting confirmation that Ye Shantao was a shareholder and director of Gongfa Company. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, Judge Lu Yimei, accompanied by Judges Zhao and Fan, opened the Civil First Tribunal for trial. First, lawyer Yan Luqing, representing more than 1,000 creditor households, stated that the main point of the appeal was to request confirmation that the appellee, Ye Shantao, was a shareholder and director of Gongfa Company. During the first trial, the appellee presented a written letter from Huang Chu'jiu, proving that Ye Shantao was not a director. The court based its judgment on this letter and ruled that he should not be held liable. Therefore, the appellants filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Court, and the first trial also acquitted Ye Shantao. Subsequently, the lawyers filed an appeal in the Second Branch of the High Court, and the judgment was announced at 1:00 PM today. The original judgment was reversed, and Ye Shantao was sentenced to three months imprisonment with a two-year reprieve for the crime of using forged documents. The forged letter from Huang Chu'jiu was confiscated. At that time, the appellee Ye Shantao was not present. His lawyer, Yu Zhongluo, stated that Ye was waiting for trial at the Third Branch of the High Court, so he was not present. However, he was still not seen in court during the trial, which shows that Ye Shantao's responsibility as a director of Gongfa Company is already beyond doubt. As for the shareholder part, it is said that it has been transferred to Ge Songxuan. Please summon Ge to the court for questioning, and it will be clear. The appellants believe that the appellee's shares have never been transferred to anyone and request the court to order the appellee to bear the responsibility of shareholder and director. Subsequently, lawyers Wang Shizong, Xu Yannian, Dong Yu, and Dong Chi, representing several thousand other creditor households, spoke successively, their reasons and wording being similar to those stated by lawyer Yan. The appellee, Ye Shantao, was represented by lawyer Lu Shaozong, who argued that the judgment of the Second Branch of the High Court had not yet been finalized because the appellee still had to file an appeal. Although the appellee was elected as a director of Gongfa Company in 1927, he never took office and had published a statement in the newspaper to that effect, and there was also a letter from Huang Chu'jiu as proof. As for the shareholder part, it had been transferred to Ge Songxuan in September 1930, and he could be summoned for questioning. The court was requested to maintain the original judgment. The successors of Zhou Songqing and Zhao Qinbo, Zhao Zengyu, Yan Wuzhi, and Yang Zhihao, represented by two lawyers, claimed that their clients were neither shareholders nor directors, and therefore they did not accept the judgment of the former French Concession court and requested an appeal to change the first trial's verdict. Lawyer Yan Luqing, representing the creditors, rose and refuted, stating that the appeal period for the claims of Zhou Songqing and the other two had passed, and the points they raised were fundamentally untenable and requested rejection. The court verified the statements and adjourned the hearing, scheduling a continuation for a later date.

Wang Jian Sentenced to Life Imprisonment

Yan Yutang, the manager of the Dalong Iron Factory, Sulun Yarn Factory, and Guangyu Business Company, from Suzhou, was kidnapped by bandits on the morning of May 4th of this year at the entrance of No. 58 Jiangxi Road. Chief Inspector Lu Liankui, Inspector Liu Shaokui, Detective Feng Zhiming, Shen Tianbao, Wang Chengying, and Wu Hanzhang of the General Investigation Department of the General Police Station successively arrested five kidnapping bandits: Wang Jian, Kong A'liu, Chen Huiqing, Chen Xiaosi, and Yang Jingzhai. The main text read: "Chen Huiqing is sentenced to death for kidnapping and extortion, and is deprived of civil rights for life. Wang Jian is sentenced to life imprisonment for kidnapping and extortion, and is deprived of civil rights for life. Kong A'liu is sentenced to sixteen years imprisonment for kidnapping and extortion, and is deprived of civil rights for life. Chen Xiaosi and Yang Jingzhai are each sentenced to six years imprisonment for assisting in kidnapping and extortion." The number of days Kong A'liu, Chen Xiaosi, and Yang Jingzhai were detained before the final judgment will be counted as two days of imprisonment for one day. Three Mauser pistols, one automatic pistol, one gas pistol, 163 Mauser bullets, 15 bullet boxes, 31 automatic bullets, two bullet boxes, and two bottles of medicine (anesthetic) are all confiscated. After the judgment was announced, Judge Qian informed the defendants that, except for Chen Huiqing (who cannot appeal under special law for those sentenced to death), if the others, such as Kong A'liu, do not accept the judgment, they can file an appeal with the Second Branch of the High Court within ten days of receiving the judgment.

Fan Zhilong Assumes Office as Director of the Jiangzhe District Fisheries Bureau Yesterday 172

Fan Zhilong, the Director of the Jiangzhe District Fisheries Administration, assumed his post at the bureau, but due to the urgency of the situation, the inauguration ceremony was not held until yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM at the bureau. Details are as follows:

Inauguration Ceremony: Present were He Bingxian, the representative of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce and the supervising official, Wen Yingxing, the Chief of the Public Security Bureau, Tang Haian, the Superintendent of the Jianghai Customs, He Hanlan, the Director of the Navigation Administration Bureau, He Zhuoxian, the Director of the Trademark Bureau, Wang Defa, the representative of the Social Affairs Bureau, and more than 200 representatives from various groups and guests. Under the supervision of the supervising official, Fan officially took office after swearing an oath. Subsequently, Wen Yingxing and Li Zhengwu delivered speeches. The ceremony concluded with a group photo and refreshments.

Supervising Official's Address: We all know that on this Earth, the area of the water world is larger and broader than the area of the land. Therefore, the products in the water are naturally very abundant. According to recent studies and surveys by biologists, there are more than 36,500 species of fish, 2,500 species of mammals, and more than 3,000 species of reptiles in the water. In addition, there are crustaceans, algae, and so on. Since there are so many types of aquatic products, the resources in the water are certainly considerable. Therefore, modern countries, in addition to developing the resources on land, have been paying attention to the water. Our eastern neighbor, Japan, with its ambitious goals, began to focus on the management of aquatic products decades ago, establishing fisheries schools, encouraging fishing, and improving the manufacture of fishing equipment. Now, Japan has become a superior aquatic product country. Speaking of our China, for thousands of years, the government and the people have not known how to strive for the great benefits of the water. The fishing methods are still old-fashioned, the fishing gear has not been improved, and the fishermen along the coast are oppressed by pirates on the one hand and invaded by foreign fishing boats on the other, so that the fishing industry has become a dying state. With the length of our country's coastline and the abundance of aquatic products, it is a pity to abandon the aquatic product industry. According to recent surveys, our country still has to import aquatic products from foreign countries (i.e., Japan, etc.) worth 140 million yuan every year. We have God-given aquatic products but do not know how to fish or use them, and instead, the rights and interests overflow to foreign countries. The loss to the national economy and the people's livelihood and foreign trade is so great that it is truly heartbreaking. The ancients said, "Goods are hated for being abandoned on the ground." Now we can say, "Goods are hated for being abandoned in the water." The National Government, in view of this, has specially divided our country's coastal areas into four fishing zones, each with a fisheries administration bureau, which is responsible for protecting fishermen and patrolling for sea bandits. Now the Jiangzhe District Fisheries Administration Bureau has been established, and today is also the day that Director Fan is sworn into office. Director Fan has expertise, and I believe that if Director Fan can implement the Ministry's fisheries administration plan and strive to protect fishermen, the aquatic product industry along the Jiangzhe coast will gradually develop, and the rights and interests will not overflow to foreign countries. This is what I personally wish for and what the government expects.

Director's Reply: Today, I am taking office, and I am very honored to have you all come to guide me. Originally, the fisheries industry occupies an important position in the industry. Even the founding strategy of the late President Sun Yat-sen paid great attention to this point. This time, I was ordered to manage the fisheries, and I will do it practically in accordance with the teachings of the President. Just now, Supervising Official He made instructions on behalf of the government, and I will sincerely accept and sincerely abide by them. As for the construction plan of fisheries that all comrades and gentlemen have instructed, I will also fully adopt them. However, my knowledge is limited. In the future, I still hope that Supervising Official He and all comrades will supervise and guide me at any time, and that would be very grateful.

Lend as Much as Possible to Revitalize Various Industries in Disaster Areas

Letter Instructs Members to Implement Original Intentions

The Shanghai Disaster Area Industry and Commerce Reconstruction Committee received a reply from the Money Trade Association yesterday, stating, "In response to your letter requesting that we inform our members to lend as much credit as possible to rescue the industrial and commercial enterprises in the disaster areas within a possible range, we hereby reply that our members are all financial enterprises and have always adhered to the principle of assisting various industries in regulating surpluses and deficits.
