Feng Bingnan's Letter to Four Organizations 174

Expresses Opposition to the Great Alliance Against Civil War

To the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, the Shanghai Banking Association, and the Money Trade Association:

I have heard that your colleagues have initiated a Great Alliance Against Civil War, hoping to eliminate internal strife and jointly resist foreign aggression. Within a month, it has resonated far and wide. How magnificent is this act, how grand is this wish! I have long admired it and am filled with praise. However, the most worrisome thing about the situation in the world is that it has become fixed. Once the situation has been formed, it is not easy to change. When it has already become chaotic, it cannot be stopped suddenly. Civil war is a chaotic phenomenon. When it occurs, it must have a source. If the source is not blocked, it is unlikely that its boiling can be stopped. Now, where is the source of civil war? Although it is called "politics for all people," the majority of people have no opportunity to participate in national affairs. The fundamental law is not established, the name and reality are inconsistent, and the gain and loss of power and position depend solely on force. Considering that the number of victories and defeats is uncertain, the distinction between obedience and disobedience is difficult to distinguish, and the world becomes private. When there is private interest, there is contention. The strong punish those who disagree, the next strongest observe the changes, and those who are not strong still think of seizing a share with a small force. This is one source. Revolution is a sudden change of progress, but the process is not always in a sudden change. Hanging it as a national policy and advocating it in learning leads to glorifying struggle. The ancients said that war is used only as a last resort, so stopping the halberd is a metaphor for military affairs, and stopping the shield is a metaphor for war. What is left for posterity is still a history of mutual slaughter. Moreover, being familiar with the propaganda of struggle and admiring the righteousness of revolution, people encourage each other, saying that it can lead to peace. Believing that the influence of the machine of nature is like a shadow following the form, the national defense army becomes a tool for personal struggle. Indulging in cruelty to the people, their courage is more than enough. Once they encounter foreign enemies, they avoid them as quickly as possible. The arrival of foreign insults often meets with internal strife. Therefore, possessing troops is not enough to defend the country, but is suitable for harming the people. This is the second source. Exploitation is used as a means of governance, and all industries are withered. Few can avoid the cold, and the lower-level people can hardly live their lives. They will not willingly sit and wait for death. The end of the Qin, Sui, Yuan, and Ming dynasties all led to their demise because of this. At that time, how could there be no people with deep knowledge and foresight who cried out loudly and tried to save the situation? However, the accumulated resentment was deep, and the unscrupulous people harbored hatred and anger to incite the people at that time. The environment at that time also drove them. Once the fire became fierce, it would not stop until it spread. This is the third source. These three sources are mutually causal. Is the disaster of civil war nearing its end? From this point of view, if the source can be blocked, there can be no war. Even if there is no anti-war, the war will stop by itself. This is the method of completely removing the firewood from under the cauldron. If this is not done, and we say "abolish war," it is like driving south while heading north. Then, should the movement to abolish war be stopped? That is not the case. As the saying goes, "To irrigate in the autumn of a great drought, the seedlings that wither later still have the merit of irrigation." Now, the great powers are surrounding us, and our neighbors are threatening us. Everyone has the humiliation of national subjugation, and everyone has the responsibility to save the country. Your association beats drums and strikes bells, awakening the deaf and enlightening the blind. Its words are strict, its righteousness is just, and its feelings are urgent and appropriate for the hearts of hundreds of millions of people. The people's spirit is manifested, and there is latent power. It depends on what the method is. If there is indeed a method to deal with this, to mend loopholes, it is as if it can be done. If its method is not incorporated into the principles, its effect will exceed what is possible. Therefore, I want to make three suggestions to your association: First, when advocating the abolition of war, we should first analyze the meaning of war and define its boundaries. The types of civil war are different. Some should be abolished, some cannot be abolished, and some cannot be allowed to be abolished. I have read Mozi's "Against Aggression" and discussed that seizing one thing and killing one person, everyone knows is unjust and criticizes it. Attacking a country harms others and benefits oneself, hinders farming and weaving, and its injustice is even greater. But they do not criticize it and instead praise it as righteous. It can be seen that the world is in chaos due to distinguishing righteousness. The words are very sad, and the "attacking a country" refers to those who invade others for profit. It should be criticized but is not criticized, which clearly shows a one-sided view, seeing the small but ignoring the big, and is actually cowardly in upholding justice. Therefore, unjust attacks are wars that should be abolished. Since then, scholars of international law have interpreted the meaning of war. Attacking and resisting each other constitutes war. Attacking without resistance, the fault lies with the aggressor. If there is no resistance, it can still be explained. Since the Charter of the League of Nations came out, it has been said that the right to protect rights can be defended by force. The arguments for self-defense are numerous, and the objective conditions are increasingly obscure. "No resistance" is a term that children know to be ridiculous. The war that is coming to attack, whether internal or external, cannot be abolished. If bandits suddenly attack and devastate cities, and communists incite and abuse, turning the land red, it is nothing but a delusion to talk about compromise. The war to suppress bandits cannot be abolished. Weigh their importance, examine their right and wrong, and then justice will exist. The Kellogg-Briand Pact's definition is unclear, and its meaning is too vague, which inevitably leads to different opinions. During its implementation, it requires too much explanation, resulting in the expected effect being invisible. The former Soviet Union's questioning of the United States is actually equal to a counter-attack. It is a lesson to be learned. Second, we should pay attention to the attitude of the military and assimilate them. For the past twenty years, internal strife has been endless, and it is almost impossible to avoid it every year. The general public has suffered terribly, and it is no wonder that they hate it deeply. Only the military is in a different situation, and it is not easy to get them to participate. However, recently, the commanders and officers have announced their rejection of civil war, which can be called an awakening. It is appropriate to take advantage of this opportunity to sincerely cooperate with them. Whether they are active-duty military officers or veterans, if they are willing to jointly initiate it, it should be adopted and the effect will be even greater. Those who are willing to be the leaders of the army should be condemned in writing and verbally, so that they have nowhere to hide. The purpose of eliminating the evil and promoting the good and subtly transforming them is what it means. Third, the alliance's solidarity should pay attention to organization. Among the gatherings of the majority of people, the most difficult thing is to be solid and lasting. The members are attached because of faith, not because of lifelong elegance. They follow because of righteousness, not because of the division between superiors and subordinates. What they have in common is the goal, and what is different is the meaning. The sages said that those who can adapt to the way cannot stand with it, and those who can stand with it cannot weigh it. To weigh with hundreds of millions of people is easy to involve in differences. If there are differences, they will be dissolved. If they are dissolved, there will be no power. If they want to be consistent in their steps and strict in their rules, it will not work without a perfect organization. The League of Nations' achievements are unsatisfactory, but its rules of deliberation and procedures for handling affairs are clearly seen in the charter, with clear outlines and detailed explanations. Its method of organization is meticulous. I do not know what the organization of your association is internally. Judging from the ten items you have put forward, it seems that it has not been perfected. If you say "no cooperation, no assistance," this is a very important declaration of sanctions. However, if the alliance itself does not have a meticulous organization, this kind of declaration is also a mere formality. It is necessary to pre-define the ways of holding meetings and so on. When specific facts occur, immediately create a plan, put it forward for discussion, analyze the reasons for the war, and evaluate the value of its use of troops. Only then can it be declared to the people of the country and extend its punishment and encouragement. If it does not undergo the above serious evaluation and makes vague remarks about sanctions, I ask, is it enough to break their hearts and weaken their morale? Ordinary lawsuits still have procedural laws to draw upon, let alone matters of public interest, where fairness is valued. If you act rashly, how can you achieve anything? Furthermore, in a country ruled by law, the general will of the people is expressed by the constitution. Therefore, the people of the whole country are moving within the orbit, and unjust wars have no chance to occur. The right to adjudicate does not belong to the free organizations. Now that the anti-war alliance has become a necessity of the times, it is clear evidence that public opinion is transformed into public power. Even if it is said that the highest authority of the state is manifested in this, it is not impossible. It is necessary to resolutely take on the responsibility of making public judgments on national affairs. This is not an excessive statement. Looking at those who have launched wars in the past, they often make explanations in their telegrams in order to win over reason. Whether they are appealing to the people or deceiving the people, it can be said that they have never completely abandoned the people in their minds. This is tantamount to acknowledging that the people have a kind of public judgment. If your association can truly fulfill its mission in this spirit, will it only receive the effect of treating the symptoms? For several years, I have never dared to seek correction from society with my remarks. I should be careful not to overstep my position in the era of political tutelage. I am just a lover of peace and deeply sympathize with the words of the benevolent. I am just expressing my feelings and attaching them to the meaning of mutual encouragement. If your association adopts them, I will be very fortunate. I respectfully wish you good health. Feng Bingnan respectfully.

Chen Lianbo to Leave Shanghai and Return to Hong Kong 175

Chen Lianbo, the former chairman of the Guangdong General Chamber of Commerce, current chairman of the Tung Wah Hospital in Hong Kong, and a prominent industrialist from the South China region, recently arrived in Shanghai from Hong Kong. Mr. Chen has long advocated and initiated numerous public welfare and charitable undertakings in various southern regions. This spring in Hong Kong, he took the lead in initiating donations to Shanghai to aid refugees displaced by war and to support the 19th Route Army, reaching over a million dollars. Overseas Chinese in various ports in Southeast Asia, Europe, and America, hearing the news, eagerly joined in fundraising to support the patriotic army. Therefore, after Mr. Chen arrived in Shanghai, the leaders of the 19th Route Army, Chen Mingshu and Cai Tingkai, held banquets for several days to welcome him. The National Disaster Relief Association, the Northeast Volunteer Army Support Association, the Guangzhao Public Association, the Guangdong Overseas Chinese Business Federation, the Shanghai Joint Association of Various Groups for National Salvation, the Overseas Chinese National Salvation Economic Committee, the Road Construction Association, the Overseas Chinese Federation, the Shanghai Guangdong Fellow Villagers Association, and other groups, as well as prominent figures such as Zhu Qinglan, Xiong Bingkun, Sun Hongyi, Chu Fucheng, and Huang Yanpei, hosted banquets one after another. Mr. Chen's visit was primarily to attend the annual shareholders' meeting of the Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company and to fulfill his mission from the Tung Wah Hospital to Shanghai, discussing with Wen Qinfu and other directors of the Guangzhao Company various issues related to the relief of war-stricken refugees. Now that the Nanyang Tobacco Company meeting has concluded, some progress has been made regarding the relief of war victims. The Guangzhao Public Association has also scheduled a welcome meeting for Mr. Chen on the 28th of this month. It is reported that Mr. Chen, having largely completed his tasks, has decided to depart Shanghai on the 29th aboard the President Jefferson and return south.

Executive Yuan Prohibits the Collection of Electricity Consumption Education Surcharge 177

The chairman of the Zhejiang Branch of the National Private Electric Power Industry Federation, Zhou Yangshan, and the vice-chairman, Han Yimin, of this organization located on Jiujiang Road in this city, previously submitted a petition to the Executive Yuan, stating that the Zhejiang Provincial Government had resolved that Yongjia County intended to collect an education surcharge on electricity consumption, which violated laws and regulations, and requested a prohibition on the collection. The Executive Yuan previously issued a directive stating, "The petition has been noted. This case has been referred to the Zhejiang Provincial Government for review. Subsequently, the reported circumstances of the case have been submitted for review and action by the Executive Yuan." It was determined that collecting a surcharge on electricity consumption was akin to levying excessive taxes, and the request for filing the record was not approved. The provincial government was instructed to swiftly forward an order to rescind the directive and comply with the filing of the record. This directive should be acknowledged.

Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Still Handled by the Ministry 178

The Ministry of Finance responded to the Jiangsu tobacco and alcohol license tax matter. Since the four groups of Shanghai Tobacco Exchange, Li Baijiu Industry, Sauce and Liquor Industry, and Sauce Garden Industry read in the newspaper that the tax would be handled by the province with increased levies, they telegraphed the Ministry of Finance to inquire about the truth. These groups received the Ministry of Finance's printed directive No. 551 yesterday, which stated, "We have received your telegram. Upon investigation, the Jiangsu tobacco and alcohol license tax case was previously approved for direct management by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, which requested direct consolidation. We immediately ordered the Finance Department to dispatch personnel to various counties to collect the tax and directly remit it to the provincial treasury." The Ministry stated that this license tax has always been directly collected by the Central Government, and all provinces have consistently followed this practice. Moreover, Article 2 of the Business Tax Law promulgated by the National Government clearly stipulates that it is a central government revenue item. The Ministry had previously replied via telegram to rescind the original proposal to avoid division and requested the Executive Yuan to issue an order to prohibit it on file. The claim in the newspaper that the Ministry approved the plan is entirely false. The associations must inform their colleagues not to easily believe rumors and cause unnecessary alarm. In addition to instructing the Jiangsu Stamp, Tobacco, and Alcohol Tax Bureau to earnestly collect taxes according to the old system, they should all comply with this directive." The associations have already recorded and circulated the order to their colleagues.

Patrolmen Abuse Authority and Extort Money 182

The Court Will Strictly Punish. Yilong in Laoximen is now newly developed by the municipal government into Heping Road. There are many small businesses setting up stalls along the roadside every morning. However, a useless patrolman named Gu Mingfu set up a stall beside a telephone pole, and Zhang Mingsan, a patrolman from the second district of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, extorted three dollars from him every week. Because of this relationship, he abused his authority to beat Gu and completely ransacked his belongings. He was detained within the district, and the whereabouts of the sold goods are unknown. Gu Mingfu lost his livelihood and was forced to petition the local court for investigation. Prosecutor Wu was ordered to investigate and dispatched personnel to conduct a clear investigation, ordering the district to return the seized property to the victim. Patrolman Zhang Mingsan was prosecuted for extortion and abuse of authority and requested to be severely punished according to the law. Yesterday morning, Judge Shi opened the court and summoned Gu Mingfu to testify. Gu stated that he was forty years old, a native of Changshu, and lived in Menglou, selling food for a living. He said, "I sell rice and vegetables and have a permit. Zhang Mingsan extorted money from me, demanding one dollar per week, otherwise, I wouldn't be allowed to set up a stall. Because of my livelihood, I paid him three dollars, which I borrowed two dollars from Shen Xiaodi. A brush seller named A Genhu saw it. It was paid on May 21st. Unexpectedly, on May 28th, he asked me again, but because the deadline had not arrived, I didn't pay. He wouldn't let me sell, kicked over the rice and vegetable bucket, and snatched my belongings. I request an investigation." Zhang Mingsan testified that he was twenty-eight years old, a native of Hefei, and served as a policeman in the second district. He stated, "I didn't ask him for money because he was obstructing traffic." The judge said, "He's a villager; if you ask him for money, would he dare not pay? Besides, he has a permit."

Page 16

The judge asked, "Since you took his things, why didn't you take him?" He replied, "He ran away." The judge said, "You're a policeman; how dare he run away?" Then he questioned the witness, A Genhu, who stated that he was twenty-eight years old, a native of Kunshan, and sold brushes at the location. There were four vegetable and rice buckets in total. He saw Gu Mingfu pay three dollars, and later he asked for three dollars again and kicked over his stall. He also paid the policeman one dollar. The judge concluded the debate in this case and instructed the policeman to come to the court on the 30th of this month to await sentencing.

Fifth Report on Cholera from the Port Quarantine Office 183

Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the Port Quarantine Office, issued the fifth weekly report on cholera, stating: (1) The prevalence of cholera in other ports has recently become almost as rampant as in Shanghai. For example, Guangzhou has exceeded 400 cases, Nanjing has exceeded 300 cases, and Tianjin has approximately 1,000 cases. In addition, Jiaxing, Suzhou, Hankou, Yantai, Qingdao, Beiping, Tanggu, Shantou, and other places have also discovered varying numbers of records of this disease. (2) The following is a list of the new cholera cases discovered up to the end of last week (June 25th), which have been bacteriologically confirmed, totaling 186 cases (including 11 deaths):

Region Patients Deaths Shanghai City 87 5 International Settlement 85 5 French Concession 14 1 Total 186 11 Previous 520 30 Total since discovery 706 41

The names of the hospitals admitting cholera patients and the number of cases are listed below:

Shanghai Epidemic Hospital 98 4 First Aid Epidemic Hospital 27 3 Hongkou Epidemic Hospital 28 0 Public Works Department Isolation Hospital 15 2 Red Cross Second Epidemic Hospital 14 2 Public Shanghai Hospital 2 0 Xinmin Road Red Cross Hospital 2 0 Total 186 11

Among the patients, there are six foreigners (one manager of a well-known German company, one British woman, one Filipino woman, one Portuguese, and two Japanese). (3) The Nanjing Health Department has supervised the health authorities of the city of Nanjing to begin testing public and private wells, numbering approximately one thousand or more, and has simultaneously undertaken disinfection work. All drinking water sources have also been subjected to bacteriological testing (because the capital does not yet have tap water facilities). It has been found that eight wells contain cholera bacteria. The well water is disinfected only with ordinary bleaching powder (containing 15 to 30 percent free chlorine) or with concentrated calcium hypochlorite, containing 65 percent free chlorine. Among those in contact with cholera in the capital, eight carriers have been isolated. Shanghai will also adopt the sanitary testing method of the capital to test natural wells and river water in order to disinfect drinking water sources. (4) The areas in Shanghai where cholera is most prevalent are listed below:

(A) Jessfield District (Caoxi Road and Zhoujia Bridge)

(B) Northwest corner of the International Settlement (surrounding Huishan Road and Xiaoshadu, near the inner and outer yarn factories)

(C) Zhabei (Tanzikou, Hujia Bridge, Xiangyan Bridge, Hongzhen, Wuzhen Bridge)

(D) Pudong (Lan Nidu, Yangjiazhai)

(E) Nanshi (Xieqiao, Jumen Road, Xietu Road, Dongjiadu)

(5) Letters have been sent to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, the Chinese Ratepayers Association, various groups and organizations, and health authorities, etc., to seek their assistance in carrying out epidemic prevention work, in order to cooperate in eradicating the epidemic. In particular, it is urgent to provide cheap or free drinking water for the general poor. This matter is not difficult, as this port does not use water trucks, which could be used to meet the urgent need. Although the tap water company and society may suffer minor losses, the difference in importance is much greater than the loss of life, the decline of the market, the disruption of shipping, and unexpected admissions to hospitals. (6) Because cholera is prevalent and rampant, all sectors of society can hardly escape it. Therefore, everyone must know that if initial symptoms such as acute diarrhea and acute vomiting are found, they should be quickly transferred to the Epidemic Hospital for diagnosis and treatment. These hospitals are specially designed to prevent and treat this disease and are well-equipped for diagnosis and effective saline injection therapy. Moreover, during a cholera epidemic, this disease is extremely difficult to treat by ordinary methods. In short, the earlier the patient is admitted to the hospital, the more hopeful it is.

The land for the Jiangwan Epidemic Hospital was donated by Mr. Zhu Jiansheng of the Flour Exchange. Last year, the directors raised a large sum of money to build a new hospital on Gong'an Road. This spring, the hospital was burned by enemy fire during the Shanghai war, and the estimated repair cost is over 2,200 dollars. In addition to raising 1,600 dollars, Xu Bingji has donated over 600 dollars to cover the shortfall, with a one-month deadline for completion. Because of the great calamity and the prevalence of epidemics, funds for annual expenses have been raised again. Once the new building is repaired, it will be moved back to its original site.

Du Shuming's Porridge Paintings 186

Mr. Du Shuming from Shaoxing (Fu Yao) is a legal expert who is also proficient in painting. He has served as a high-level prosecutor and presiding judge in Jiangsu and Shanghai. He is talented by nature and began painting plum blossoms at a young age. The elders Zhou Yushan and Tang Dianxian praised him highly, comparing him to Wang Yuanzhang and Liu Xuehu. Later, he also became skilled in painting flowers and plants, which were vivid and colorful, all appearing at the tip of his brush. It is truly a wonder that his brushwork rivals the ancients and he can participate in the creation of nature. For many years, he served in the legal field without neglecting painting. His art has improved greatly. People who have obtained his inch-sized or foot-long paintings treasure them like priceless jade. At the request of friends, he has exhausted the porridge in Shanghai to share his art with those who love it. Those who are interested in tasting it in China should be among the first to see it. The contemporary celebrity Yu Youren has also written the price list for him, and major fan shops are collecting submissions on his behalf.

Four-Year-Old Girl Falls into Well 187

Xu Fusheng, a local resident of Hujia Bridge at the Yangshupu Water and Electricity Plant, had a four-year-old daughter who suddenly disappeared on the 18th of this month. It was rumored that she was abducted by Ye Yonggen and Li Hosheng. On the 24th, Jiang, Li, and Ye were brought to the police station and transferred to the court. However, because there was no evidence, they were released. Unexpectedly, the day before yesterday, someone went to draw water from the well at the house and suddenly saw a child's body. They immediately pulled it up and found that it was Xu's missing daughter. Xu was notified and was greatly saddened. He went to the police station to report that she had been murdered. Yesterday, the local headman reported it to the local court for an autopsy. Prosecutor Zhao and others confirmed that she had drowned and ordered an investigation into the cause of death.

Shanghai Office of "Five Bees Magnesium Carbonate" 190

The Ningbo Chaiqiao Five Bees Magnesium Carbonate Factory was established in 1922. It hires specialized chemical technicians to produce magnesium carbonate, a chemical industrial raw material and a daily necessity for medical and health purposes, using "Five Bees" as a registered trademark. Since its establishment, it has been widely sold throughout the country, resisting imported goods, regaining rights and interests, and assisting the rapid development of the chemical industry and new drug industry operated by Chinese people. Its effectiveness is immense. In the past, it has entrusted other companies to act as distributors in Shanghai, but it has not been able to promote the product vigorously. It has been reported that the factory has dispatched specialists to Shanghai to develop its business and facilitate customers. It has established an office at No. 2, Dongxing Lane, Danfeng Road, Xiaodongmen, to directly contact all sectors and welcome factories to purchase and use their products.

Summary of the Jinghui Canal Project 191

The Jinghui Canal in Weibei, Shaanxi, held its completion ceremony on the 20th of this month. The total cost of the project was over 900,000 national currency. The design and construction were carried out by Mr. Lu Er'kang, an engineer of the China International Famine Relief Commission, who wrote an article published in the Engineering Quarterly, Volume 6, No. 4. The recently published Engineering Weekly, No. 10, also contains an article by Mr. Li Yizhi on the engineering construction of Shaanxi, summarizing its key points. This is an introduction for those who are concerned about the construction of the Northwest. Both the Engineering Quarterly and the Engineering Weekly are published by the Chinese Institute of Engineers. The Quarterly costs 3 jiao per issue, and the Weekly costs 1 dollar per year. The subscription office is located on the 5th floor of the Mainland Shopping Center on Nanjing Road in this city.

Women's Christian Association Labor Department Epidemic Prevention Campaign 192

The Labor Department of the local Women's Christian Association, because of the multitude of factories in Shanghai, workers often disregard hygiene. Now that the summer season is abnormal and the tiger epidemic is prevalent, if no measures are taken to guide and prevent it, it will inevitably spread everywhere in the future, making relief even more difficult. Therefore, the department's workers' groups specially held a hygiene sports meeting at the Huxi Women Workers' Community last week. In addition to inviting members of the Municipal Health Bureau to lecture on summer hygiene methods and administer vaccinations, there were also recreational activities such as ventriloquism, film screenings, singing, and hygiene performances. The order of the meeting was entirely handled by the group members. After the meeting, the group members were also instructed to go out and distribute leaflets in various public alleys (such as methods for health and longevity, eliminating flies, the scourge of humanity, etc.) and lecture on public health and methods for preventing tiger epidemics. It is reported that 260 people attended that day, and 230 people received vaccinations.

Army Commander Cai Commends Yong An Tang 193

Since the unfortunate incident in Shanghai, Mr. Hu Wenhu, a prominent overseas Chinese businessman in Singapore, was the first to advocate and assist in donating funds, and the amount raised was quite substantial. Recently, it was learned that Mr. Hu Guigeng, the newly appointed general manager of Hu's Tiger Balm Yong An Tang in Shanghai, acting on Mr. Hu's instructions, paid a special visit to Mr. Cai Tingkai, the army commander of the 19th Route Army, and reported the donation and fundraising accounts in detail. Army Commander Cai personally inscribed the words "Medicine for Saving the World" to commend the company. It is also reported that the company has recently found premises at 595 Ningbo Road as a distribution point for the purpose of developing its business. Furthermore, because the company's Tiger Balm, Bagua Dan, Qingkuai Water, Headache Powder, and other medicines are urgently needed for summer hygiene, they are being sold in advance at that location.

William's Pharmacy Subsidized Staff Thanked for Disaster Relief 194

Many of the staff of William's Pharmacy in Shanghai reside in the Zhabei and Hongkou areas. As a result, many of them lost their furniture and clothing in the Japanese bombardment in February. The pharmacy, on the instructions of its Canadian headquarters manager and board of directors, issued substantial subsidies to these staff members to provide assistance. Therefore, 4,696 Shanghai dollars have already been distributed. Last Saturday (the 25th), the staff members who received these subsidies sent representatives to visit Mr. Wu Lifu, the general manager of the Shanghai branch, to express their gratitude. Mr. Xu Weigong, the Chinese manager who has been with the company for 24 years, requested Mr. Wu to convey their thanks to the manager and board of directors of the Canadian headquarters. In addition, it is worth noting that most of the Chinese staff members of the pharmacy have been with the company for a long time. Among them, two have been working since the Shanghai branch opened 24 years ago. Many others have been working for 23, 22, 20, or more than 16 years. Mr. Wu Lifu, the general manager of the Shanghai branch, has been serving the pharmacy in various locations, including South Africa, Singapore, and China, for as long as 37 years.

Chen Yunquan, Jin Fuchun, Zhu Zhixian, and other executive committee members of the Yongyi Charity Hall in Caojiadu, Huxi, in view of the severe battles this year and the repeated outbreaks of tiger epidemics everywhere, and because the town is vast and densely populated, believe that the epidemic will inevitably be more severe than in the past. His spare time verses are exceptional,

One sees a naturalness that is startling.

He's not the second person in the poetry arena. (Zeng Wenzheng)

Eastern Prefecture's Three Excellences: painting, poetry, calligraphy,

Washing away the makeup, retaining the original color,

Beyond the form, he learns from Su, the whiskered elder. (He Zizhen)

A teacher who doesn't strive for perfection is just a teacher,

Du Fu's ballads are all laments of the times. (Zheng Ziyin)

Science

Mr. Einstein Gives Up Curved Space 201

— Gao Qian

Mr. Einstein, the creator of the theory of relativity, argued that space is curved, finite, and that a beam of light sent out can go around a big circle and come back. His theory shook the world.

But now, Mr. Einstein has abandoned his concept of curved space.

According to Mr. Einstein's opinion, space is probably infinite, three-dimensional, and light rays sent out will not return, which is the same as what scientists have always assumed. However, this change in concept has no impact on the truth of the theory of relativity.

There are several reasons why Mr. Einstein abandoned his curved space concept.

First, the observations from the Wilson Mountain Observatory show that the light bands of distant nebulae move towards the red end. The farther the nebula, the greater the movement. This proves that the universe is expanding constantly, and the rate of expansion is surprisingly high, 150,000 miles per second! Mr. Einstein used to think that space was finite, so in order to complete his theory, he assumed that space was curved. As for this expanding space, he had never thought of it.

Second, Dr. Heckman of Göttingen University in Germany has proved that expanding space can contain matter and still be Euclidean. Based on this hypothesis, Mr. Einstein abandoned his curved space argument.

Based on this new concept, Mr. Einstein can calculate the density of space using the equations in his theory of relativity. However, this density is smaller than we imagined. On average, there is only one pound of matter in a large empty sphere sixty times the diameter of the Earth. Space is constantly expanding, so the density is still decreasing day by day.

(Note) The material for this article is taken from the May 7th "DlitraryDigest" in the United States.

A Corner of Society

Snatching the Oily Perch 202

— Ying Dai

If you see a row of old houses on the side of the road with a new bamboo fence erected outside, then the houses are about to be demolished. After a considerable period of time, after the bamboo fence is removed, a row of new houses will suddenly appear before your eyes. The new houses naturally have new tenants, and if the house is close to the road, then many new shops will open next.

New shops, no matter what kind, will always sell things cheaper on the first day than the old shops. Although they may not be willing to lose money, it can be determined that they cannot make money that day. Therefore, the first day of business for a new shop is always very lively, and all the employees are always extremely busy and have to ask many people to help.

It is said that there are rules for new shops. The first person, holding a red paper packet in his hand, containing very little money, wants to buy very valuable things. The friends in the shop are not allowed to refuse him. So, two cents buys a pack of Golden Mouse cigarettes, four cents buys a ham, etc. Jokes like these are often heard on the first day of a new shop.

But if you want to be the first to walk into the door of the new shop and buy something very cheap and especially cheap, then you have to get up the night before and wait at the door of the shop. If you don't believe it, look, when the door of the new shop has not been removed, there are already many customers waiting outside. The first group of people get up early in the dark to prepare to snap up cheap goods. But if you want to be the first to run into the shop door, you must have strength, otherwise you will be pushed out of the crowd, and you will never be able to squeeze into the crowd.

Going to a new shop to buy cheap goods is called "snatching the oily perch." We also have this kind of rule in our hometown. When a new row of shops opens in a town, people from all over the countryside come to snatch the oily perch. They are far from the town, but they are waiting at the door before dawn, so you know they get up the night before. I remember when I was a child, a new butcher shop opened across from my house. A friend slept at the door the night before. The next day, when the butcher shop opened, he was the first to go in and bought a pig's leg for two cents. Jokes like these are often heard.

In Shanghai, as soon as a new shop opens, the old nanny tells the old lady, the young lady tells the nanny, the chauffeur tells the young master, the little brother and sister tell their mother. The news will spread quickly. So, on the day of the opening, the customers are always as lively as they can be.

Chinese merchants, especially in Shanghai, are extraordinarily jealous. If one shop sells cheap goods, the competitors will immediately compete with them. New shops are also the same. If a new shop opens, the competing shops on the same road will also hang lanterns and streamers, play military music, and sell their cheap goods. Recently, a new pharmacy opened on Xinza Road. The nearby competitors also hung lanterns and streamers and sold cheap goods in the same way, but there were very few customers. It was not as lively as other types of shops. Taking medicine is originally an unlucky thing. If you are not sick, who would go to snatch the oily perch? At the same time, I am reminded that if a coffin shop opens, maybe no one will go to snap up cheap goods.

The Problem of Bread

Graduates' Way Out 203

— Bai Shui

Mr. C, who is busy with graduation exams, only came to my house for a chat the night before last. Naturally, I couldn't help but congratulate him. I asked him:

"Four years of university life, today can be considered the end! That must be your proudest day!"

"What are you talking about? I just survived four years and finished a section!" he said.

"Then, are you going to the East or the West?" I asked him again.

"It's not easy to talk about. Not to mention going abroad to study, I don't even have a way out right now!" he said.

"Those are just polite words," I glanced at him, with a somewhat believing and somewhat disbelieving attitude, and asked him again.

Then he was silent for a while, and then, frowning, he solemnly replied to me:

"Alas! Old classmate, let's not talk polite words! Not to mention anything else, it has taken us such families a lot of effort to get a university degree! Still thinking about going abroad? That's just a dream! Look, recently classmate K went to M City. I heard that his relatives have immediately found him a good job, so he's going there to take up his new post! Classmate L also went to K City, but I'm the only one still wandering at the crossroads. The other day, I ran into an old classmate, Mr. W, whom I hadn't seen for five years. He is the director of the political department of the XX Army, and he's going to F Province to suppress bandits soon. Maybe there's a way out there? But I was born with a very solitary nature. On the one hand, I can't get used to the life in the army, and on the other hand, I don't want to step into the class with guns. But if I don't go, these major problems of food, clothing, and shelter cannot be solved. Alas! It's really depressing!"

"He paused for a while and continued to say to me: Now, I regret that I studied! If my parents hadn't taught me to study, like my uncle's son, I would be farming and planting vegetables at home every day, which would be so happy. But what about me? I spend eight hundred yuan a year and waste a lot of precious time, but in the end, I can't find a way out. Isn't that a joke? Alas! In the final analysis, it's all the bad social environment that makes us graduates panic about unemployment!"

After hearing these words, I naturally expressed a lot of sympathy in my heart. In fact, how many people in Chinese society are feeling the same pain as Mr. C right now? I think; in this society where politics is not on the right track, the standards for employing people are chaotic. No matter how talented and knowledgeable you are, if you don't have those key figures in the political arena to promote you, I'm afraid you'll be buried for decades and still can't raise your head! Alas! "Graduates' Way Out"

Living in a Dream, Dying in a Dream

Opium, Mahjong, and Feasts 204

— Hao Ying

A narrow and pitifully small Baoshan City, | our hometown, was still in the pockets of the enemy a month ago; now, we can finally freely enter and exit and live peacefully in our own broken houses that have been pierced by artillery shells.

The houses are empty. Finding a pair of chopsticks and a broken eating bowl is simply a dream. What we have are high piles of garbage outside the walls, and several volumes of magazines abandoned by the "enemy" in the grass piles in the yard.

I curiously picked up that volume of Japanese magazine with more than 500 pages and flipped through it page by page. Needless to say, the rich materials and large number of illustrations in it cannot be found in any first-rate magazine in China. In particular, the research on the three northeastern provinces of China. On the other hand, the magazine published many illustrations ridiculing China. Although I don't understand Japanese and cannot fully understand the text annotating these illustrations, what the illustrations indicate to me, and the occasional Chinese characters in Japanese, are enough to provide a stimulus for someone worn out by chaos!

We only need to pick one to talk about: The topic is "Chinese Y Faces (Prestige)" It depicts a person who looks exactly like an old Chinese gentleman. A melon-skin cap and old glasses are indispensable. He is wearing a huge black mandarin jacket, hunched over his back, and has his hands folded on the table. In front of him are three indispensable living materials: a smoking pipe, mahjong tiles, and big fish.

In a short paragraph explaining the illustrations, one can still find these phrases piecemeal: "::Senior officials:: One day:: Few:: Two or three banquets." "Mahjong:: Opium:: Also they:: Important components of life::"

What beautiful faces of the Chinese people! Here, there is enough for us to ponder!

This is indeed the truth; First, the power of Mahjong to penetrate Chinese society is even more universal than Danish education. Whether illiterate women, underdeveloped children, noble (!) officials, or humble (!) carters, they will all pull up four companions for another four rounds. This widespread gambling tool has not only become a wonderful item for social interaction and a tool for leisure, but among the general idle class it has become almost as important a condition of life as food, clothing, and shelter! Second, although opium is not as popular as Mahjong in China, the total number of smokers, when counted, is bound to be huge and astonishing. Taking our Baoshan City, with a population of five or six thousand, as an example, there are already more than forty "swallow nests." Others who smoke and burn themselves are not included. Each "swallow nest" has an average of ten regular customers, which amounts to four or five hundred people! Baoshan is like this, but other places such as Sichuan, Anhui, Shaanxi, Hebei, and Fujian, where poppies are grown, even women and children smoke them, then Baoshan's achievements are far behind! Third, regarding banquets with big fish and big meat, the daily newspaper reports about officials inviting guests and holding banquets, and capitalists drinking and eating wildly, will really make people forget all the difficult and shameful encounters. General "political maniacs," petty politicians, and junior officials often use inviting guests (of course, lavish and beautiful) as a stepping stone to advancement or as a means of ingratiation. Others, such as weddings, funerals, and celebrations among the people, always hold several or dozens of tables of grand banquets, inviting relatives and friends to feast. With all this, the Japanese satirize us: Taking opium, playing mahjong, and holding big fish and big meat banquets as a matter of face, do we still have room to defend ourselves?

Friends! Has everyone lived through this era? Have you seen the current environment? Can we continue like this forever?

Page 18

Having

Finished Reading "The Road" 205

— Yan Meng

During the bitter plum rains of several days, in my depression, I finished reading Mao Dun's "The Road." Mao Dun used to report on overseas literary news in "Short Story Monthly". At that time, everyone did not know that he was a great Chinese genius. Later, because he participated in the political movement, he saw a lot of things, so all the revolutionary and morbid facts became his complex subject matter. By the time his trilogy was completed, the literary world exclaimed in unison at his descriptive skills.

My brother Ji Cheng is very familiar with him. They used to be colleagues at the Commercial Press, and later they were jointly responsible for editing the "Literary Ten-Day Magazine" at the Literary Research Association. According to him: "Mao Dun writes novels so powerfully, largely because he was influenced by the French writer Maupassant." I believe this very much, and I think Mao Dun himself would admit this.

"The Road" is also one of Mao Dun's recent works, but it is not as profound as "Disillusionment", "Hesitation", and "Pursuit". The materials are not as rich and moving as the trilogy. However, compared to the many works that waste paper and ink in vain, "The Road" is still a good novel worth publishing. In the youth consciousness of being at a loss, he still grasped the soul of the times, he found a way out for some young people between the dead ends!

Politics is not on the right track, and there is nothing to be done. The education sector, which has been in turmoil almost every day for several years, is unfolding in the same way as the warlords' civil war. Inside, we see the crisis of Chinese education, we see the moral bankruptcy of educators; the children to be saved are struggling in the water and fire with unrestrained enthusiasm. They | the young students | are neither good at making plans nor can they compromise. So he, Xin | the protagonist of the novel, is skeptical with tears in his eyes. After the first wave of unrest, he is passive and pessimistic; the second time, he becomes mad and desperate. He knows that it is all wrong, "Be tenacious, neither passive nor mad. A war of attrition"!

The impatience of the youth is a mess.

Xin said: "Sacrifice is nothing. There are many people like that. It's no good for me at all." The gray society! The gray nation is waiting for the youth's hot blood to be defiled and washed away!

Xin asked Du Ruo: "Don't you love me?"

"Love! It's my own way of loving. It can let you love for a while!" Du Ruo answered him. The romantic love view of modern girls is true. Mao Dun is very sure about the analysis and dissection of all kinds of things. About our motherland's current tribulations, what efforts should we writers make in literature and thought to find our way?
